Current Affairs Commentary

What Are the Reasons Company Stocks Cannot Circulate?

— Qing

A few days ago, this newspaper's current affairs commentary discussed the problem of industrial and commercial enterprises absorbing capital. It stated that our country's company stocks have no public market prices or circulation mechanisms. Those seeking them find it difficult to find them, and those selling them find it difficult to sell them, making them securities that cannot circulate. This is indeed the current situation of most company stocks in our country. However, what are the reasons for this? Please allow us to conduct a historical review of this point.

The beginning of the securities industry in our country was initially promoted under the name of "joint-stock companies." During the early stages of the European War, Chinese industry flourished for a time, and stock trading was quite prosperous. At that time, company stocks such as the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Ning Shao Company, Dasheng Yarn Factory, Commercial Press, and Hanyeping Company were very active in the market. The lively state remains deeply imprinted on our minds. Government bond trading, on the other hand, was limited by the limited number of issues and only occupied a secondary position. However, before long, the European War ended. The once-prosperous industries mostly suffered a severe setback. As a result, the foundation of the stock market was almost completely destroyed. Government bond trading then took its place and monopolized the market. When the stock market crash occurred, investors, deceived by the lure of high profits, eagerly tried to encompass all to meet them, but unexpectedly suffered a crushing defeat and their funds were thrown into a bottomless pit. General investors had to become somewhat cautious as a result.

The disappearance of company stocks from the market was indeed due to the times and the environment. However, the loss of credit due to the poor management of some companies was also an important reason. In the past, when the China National Sugar Manufacturing Company was established, the founders issued a rallying cry, and investors were very enthusiastic. Even people from the inland areas came to Shanghai, often traveling extra distances, to request to buy shares, hoping that the people's interest in investment would gradually be aroused. Unexpectedly, due to poor planning in advance and the failure of the organizers, it fell into an irreparable state before it even officially started construction. Although various plans have been made over the past ten years, there has been no way to revive it. As for those who were once known for their excellent business performance, but suffered irreparable losses due to the organizers not following the usual practices and expanding excessively, there are many examples. These failures in industry and commerce are enough to affect the credit of all corporate enterprises. This is why company stocks in our country are not easily circulated today.

Moreover, in recent years, due to the general enthusiasm of businessmen for speculation, the securities market has relied on the futures trading of government bonds as its lifeline. Spot trading is just a formality and insignificant. Stock trading is even more disregarded. We previously heard that people outside the industry were forming another stock exchange, but because stocks were hastily put up for auction, there were many types of spot trading, and few transactions. Before half a month had passed, it had returned to being an exchange with prices but no market. The numerous names of company stocks and the different content of each company mean that not only do the general public lack a deep understanding of them, but even securities practitioners probably lack the knowledge to study them. There are also no such reference publications available. Investors have no way to ask for information. How can investment interest be aroused?

If we want company stocks to become active in the market again in the future, we should start by reducing the speculative mentality of general businessmen and establishing the social credit of those engaged in real industry.

The Qichin and Liangchen Warships are Incorporated into the Third Fleet, Xie Gangzhe Arrives in Beijing to Ask for Instructions

(Nanjing) Third Fleet Commander Xie Gangzhe, because the Qichin and Liangchen warships have been ordered by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to be incorporated into the Third Fleet and temporarily stationed in the Yangtze River, came to Beijing from Guangdong to discuss the matter. He arrived in Beijing on the morning of the 14th. That evening, the commander's representative in Beijing held a banquet. In the evening, the captains of the Qichin and Liangchen warships held a banquet to welcome Xie. Xie will return to Qingdao after the matters concerning the two warships are discussed in Beijing. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 14th)

(Qingdao) Reliable sources say that Third Fleet Commander Xie Gangzhe took the first Jiaoji Railway train to Ji'nan at 9:00 PM on the 12th, and then transferred to Beijing to ask the Central Government for instructions on the matter of transferring the Qichin and Liangchen warships to the jurisdiction of the Third Fleet. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 14th)

(Nanjing) Third Fleet Commander Xie Gangzhe was ordered to transfer the Haiqin and Haiqi warships to the command of his fleet. He came from Qingdao to ask for instructions on the procedures for joining the fleet and to report on defense matters. He arrived in Beijing on the morning of the 14th. In the afternoon, he visited Zhu Peide, Chen Ce, and others to report and ask for instructions on everything. (Special dispatch on the 14th)

The Soviet Journalist Delegation Continues to Petition Yesterday

(Nanjing) The petition delegation of newspaper reporters from various counties in Jiangsu Province gathered at the Central Hotel at 7:00 AM on the morning of the 14th. They set off at 7:30 AM and went to the Central Political Council to petition. It was during a meeting, so Ye Chucang, a member of the Standing Committee, received them. The representatives presented their petition. Ye said that all of it would be accepted, and that the case had been handed over to the Legislative Group of the council for review, which would be instructed to send the principle back to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration. The representatives asked how much the amendments could be. Ye replied that since amendments were being prepared, they would be amended thoroughly. He said that the opinions put forward by the press from various places could be amended separately. He said that he had been a newspaper reporter before, and would not forget the sufferings of reporters just because he was no longer a reporter. The representatives expressed their satisfaction. They then asked Ye to preside over the matter from beginning to end. Ye replied that he was willing to be a representative for everyone, hoping to satisfy everyone. The representatives expressed their satisfaction. They then went to the Judicial Yuan to petition, asking for an interpretation of the criminal law on publication, and the issue of multiple penalties for reporters' errors. Secretary Xie Guansheng received them and promised to forward the representatives' opinions to President Ju. The representatives returned to their residences at 11:00 AM. In the afternoon, at 2:30 PM, the delegation again sent representatives and, together with the Capital Journalism Society and reporters stationed in Beijing from Tianjin, Shanghai, and Wuhan, formed three groups, carrying a joint petition statement signed by the three expanded petition groups. The three groups set off for the Legislative Group of the Central Political Council and the Central Committee members in Beijing to conduct an expanded petition. The first group, consisting of Cheng Qi, Zhao Ying, Shen Jiuxiang, Sun Dexian, and Hu Juemin, visited Chen Gongbo, Ma Chaojun, and Jiao Yitang, but none of them were present. They left the statement of the three groups. The second group, consisting of Zhao Minheng, Liao Shouchang, and Bao Mingshu, visited Shao Yuanchong, Ye Chucang, Zhu Jiahua, Luo Jialun, Ye Li, and Luo, but none of them were present. They met Shao Yuanchong, who expressed sympathy for the opinions put forward by the reporters and promised to do his best to mediate when the Legislative Group of the Central Political Council held a meeting to review them. The third group, consisting of Chen Mingde, Sun Zhaokai, Cao Dazong, and Wang Shenwu, visited Wang Shijie, Gu Zhenggang, Qin Zhen, and Deng Feihuang. Qin Dengmin was out and not present. Wang said that he accepted all the statements submitted by the three groups and promised to bring them up for discussion at the Legislative Group meeting. Gu said that public opinion was the spirit of the people, and at a time when the people's morale was declining, the government should especially enhance the authority of public opinion and promote the people's morale. The press should also cooperate effectively with the government. He believed that the amendments requested by the press were very legitimate and was willing to support them. Finally, Gu added that the Legislative Group of the Central Political Council had recently exchanged views and believed that the amendments to the publication law this time were excessive and did not conform to the principles previously set by the Legislative Group. It was necessary to re-establish the principles and send them back to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration. His words were very sincere and moved the representatives. They returned in the evening. Also, the Jiangsu county petition delegation decided to form the Jiangsu Journalism Society. In addition to the three counties of Zhenjiang, Wuxi, and Wuxian, which were originally assigned to be responsible for the preparation, six additional counties, Wujin, Jiangyin, Changshu, Yixing, Jiangdu, and Nantong, were added to participate in the preparation. Also, the three counties of Zhenjiang, Wuxi, and Wuxian were elected as standing committee members of the preparatory committee. The location of the preparatory committee was temporarily set in Wuxi. All preparatory matters and the aftermath of the petition will be handled by Wuxi. 4. All the representatives of this petition in Beijing will be the initiators of the Jiangsu Journalism Society, and the preparatory committee will submit an application to the Jiangsu Provincial Party Department in the name of all the initiators for registration. (Special dispatch on the 14th)

Ministry of Interior Explains Ambiguities in the Law on Punishment of Violations of Public Order

(Nanjing) The Fujian Provincial Government stated that the Law on Punishment of Violations of Public Order stipulates that if a hotel knows that a guest is about to commit a serious crime under criminal law and does not secretly report it to the public security bureau, it should be punished. Now that the new criminal law has been implemented on July 1, there is no such provision, and there is no doubt about its applicability. The Ministry of Interior explained that since Article 33, Section 4 of the Law on Punishment of Violations of Public Order is based on Article 162 of the old criminal law, although the new criminal law has deleted that article, it should still be punished according to the crime level standards stipulated in the old criminal law before the Law on Punishment of Violations of Public Order is amended. As for those who have violated the crime stipulated in Article 162 of the old criminal law, although it does not constitute a crime under the new criminal law, it should still be punished for violating public order because it has a great impact on social order, in order to maintain public security. The Ministry of Interior replied to the Fujian Provincial Government on the 14th, and also notified all provinces and cities to investigate. (Special dispatch on the 14th)

Yuan Lianghua Arrives in Beijing to Report to the Ministry of Industry on Fisheries Administration

(Nanjing) Yuan Lianghua, Director of the Fisheries Protection Office of the Ministry of Industry, arrived in Beijing on the morning of the 14th to discuss fisheries protection matters with the Maritime Department and report to the Ministry of Industry on fisheries administration. Yuan said that the Shanghai fish market project has been completed to 90%. It is scheduled to start operations at the beginning of next month. In terms of capital, it was originally a joint public-private venture, with government shares of 500,000 yuan, which has been allocated by the Ministry of Industry. Due to the economic downturn, private shares could not be paid up. The Ministry of Industry has provided another 500,000 yuan, and the remainder may continue to be allocated by the Ministry in succession. The future operating system will follow the Japanese Central Wholesale Market method, adopting a brokerage system. Various regulations and the number of brokers are being reviewed. The commission for fishermen is proposed to be 10%, with the brokers and the market splitting it equally. At the same time, in order to adjust the capital of the fishing grounds, the market will borrow a large amount of money from the banking industry to lend to fishermen, which is also being negotiated. (Special dispatch on the 14th)

Hunan Province Requests Funds for Emergency Relief

Qingdao Fishery and Salt Experiment Zone to be Established

(Nanjing) The Qingdao Fishery and Salt Experiment Zone, which was planned by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, is almost ready and will be established within a few days. The articles of association and the main points of the system will be organized by one representative each from the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, and one local fisheries officer. The duties are: (1) Matters related to the experiment and research of fishery and salt; (2) Matters related to the allocation of local salt affairs organs and the guidance of the distribution of fishery salt; (3) Matters related to the research on improving fishery supervision and sales; (4) Matters related to the investigation of the purchase and use of salt by the fishery industry; (5) Other experimental matters. The experimental period is temporarily set at two years. (Special dispatch on the 14th)

To Save the East African War, Eden Arrives in Paris with a Plan, The Tripartite British, French, and Italian Conference Opens Today, Seeking a Solution from an Economic Perspective

(Paris) The tripartite conference on Abyssinia will open tomorrow with an eagerness that is not marred by undue pessimism or optimism, according to a person in charge who spoke to a Reuters reporter. However, the opinion of one group of people is mostly pessimistic, and it is widely felt that Britain holds the key to solving this problem. However, no one but Eden now knows what proposals Britain will have. Eden arrived here last night. Many news reporters were waiting for him. Eden did not make a statement and drove to the British Embassy.

According to Reuters from London, Britain will pay close attention to the tripartite talks. British public opinion generally knows the far-reaching consequences that the Italian-Abyssinian war will cause. Britain now believes that although the Italian-Abyssinian dispute is difficult and has reached a critical stage, there is still a way to solve it if it can return to a point of calm and reasonable research. It is hoped that the tripartite talks will achieve this goal. The British government has thoroughly studied all aspects of the overall situation in the past few weeks, and the economic aspect has also been involved. Therefore, Eden will be able to put forward constructive suggestions for the representatives to discuss. This suggestion will not apply pressure to either side of the dispute and will be of great benefit to the work of agreeing on a plan that can be accepted by both sides. At present, there are two possible courses of action, peace or war. If a peaceful resolution is not sought, then force will inevitably be resorted to, regardless of the repeated treaty obligations, and the instability in Europe will be even worse. The value of all international contracts will then be questioned, and this point alone will be enough to cause a reaction from various races in remote areas, which will be irreparable. It is expected that the tripartite conference will be chaired by French Prime Minister Laval, and the Italian representative will be Baron Aloisi. The results of the conference will be reported to the League of Nations Executive Council meeting on September 4. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

Anglo-French Talks Begin: Eden States British Viewpoint; Offers Economic Interests, Opposes Political Cessions

(Paris) The British and French delegations held their first talks at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 11:00 this morning to discuss the Italian-Abyssinian issue, concluding at 12:15. The British side was represented by Minister Without Portfolio Anthony Eden, British Ambassador to France Sir Eric Phipps, and Permanent Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs Sir Robert Vansittart. The French side was represented by Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Pierre Laval, Director of Political Affairs at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Mr. Berthelot, and Principal Private Secretary, Mr. Rochat. Laval then issued a statement to the press, saying that he would meet with Italian representative Aloisi tomorrow, and a formal meeting with Eden and Aloisi would be held on Friday. (Havas, 14th)

(Paris) According to information obtained by a Havas diplomatic correspondent, when British Minister Without Portfolio Anthony Eden held talks with Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Pierre Laval this morning, Eden only stated the British view on the Italian-Abyssinian dispute to Laval. The British government advocates establishing an agreement on Abyssinia based on the Tripartite Treaty of 1906 regarding Abyssinia and the exchange of notes between Great Britain and Italy on December 20, 1925. The exchange of notes between Great Britain and Italy on December 20, 1925, allowed all countries with connections to Abyssinia to obtain equal opportunities for economic development, but political preferences should be rejected. The official also said that Italy should be allowed to have a large sphere of influence in Abyssinia to engage in economic development, but the areas along Lake Tana and the upper reaches of the Nile River and its tributaries should be reserved as a sphere of British interest. The principles stipulated in this declaration could have led to the conclusion of a treaty, but the Abyssinian government did not agree to the draft treaty, so it was abandoned. Currently, Britain does not want to obtain any new interests in Abyssinia and is prepared to support Italy's economic demands, but Britain opposes political concessions, because Abyssinia is an independent country and a member of the League of Nations. If its territorial integrity is once destroyed, it will inevitably endanger the collective security system based on the League of Nations. As for Laval, he strongly advocated that the Italian-Abyssinian dispute must be resolved peacefully, otherwise it may inevitably lead to serious international consequences. The content of today's Anglo-French talks is roughly like this. After the Italian representative Aloisi arrives in Paris tomorrow, he can present the main viewpoints of the Italian government to Laval. The formal negotiations will not begin until the three countries hold a meeting on Friday. (Havas, 14th)

(Paris) Sir Anthony Eden arrived here last night and will hold preliminary talks with Foreign Minister Laval this morning. Le Matin hopes that the talks between the two can clarify whether Britain is prepared to concede economic interests to Italy to resolve the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, or still refuses to consider a political solution to Italy's demands. Le Journal says that the British suggestion of redistributing colonies is impossible, but it is hoped that a constructive plan can be put forward, allowing Italy to obtain some economic interests in Abyssinia. However, the newspaper is ambiguous about whether Italy is willing to accept this solution, because Italy has repeatedly stated that political and military control of Abyssinia is necessary. (National News Agency, 14th)

(Paris) A London dispatch says that Sir Anthony Eden will bring an important plan to resolve the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, which has attracted attention here. Eden is expected to arrive here tonight, and political circles here are eagerly awaiting him. It is widely rumored that Eden will advocate the redistribution of colonies to save the Italian-Abyssinian war. Le Journal states that Britain must bear the cost of this proposal and cede a part of British Somaliland to Abyssinia. Le Quotidien says that this proposal should not be taken seriously, because this proposal may not be more advanced than the one Eden recently proposed to Mussolini in Rome. (National News Agency, 13th)

(Paris) The tripartite Anglo-French-Italian conference to discuss the Italian-Abyssinian dispute is about to be held. According to what Le Matin's correspondent in London knows, the British delegation has been ordered to seek an economic solution that can be accepted by both Italy and Abyssinia. The current situation of the Italian-Abyssinian dispute is better than in recent days. At that time, British cabinet members advocated that the tripartite conference should only study the clauses from a legal point of view (referring to the Anglo-French-Italian Treaty of 1906) and should not go beyond the scope of interpreting the clauses. But now this attitude has changed. The reason is that Minister Without Portfolio Anthony Eden has pointed out that if European countries fail to mediate the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, the impact on the League of Nations and the collective security system will be very serious. According to what Le Matin's correspondent knows, Eden has been ordered to act as he sees fit, but the government still urges him to be cautious. Furthermore, according to Le Journal's correspondent in London, "When British Minister Without Portfolio Anthony Eden discusses the Abyssinian issue with Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval today, he intends to put forward a strong theory to persuade France to listen, that is, if France does not support Britain's views and does not oppose the Italian-Abyssinian conflict, the European collective security system will suffer a fatal blow. Britain will retreat behind the scenes, and even if France is threatened by Germany, it will not come to France's aid. As for the work of maintaining Austria's independence, Britain will also turn a blind eye to it. In short, Britain will no longer resist the German-Austrian merger and will allow Germany to act freely. The above news is now no longer concealed by people in the British capital." (Havas, 14th)

Report on the Achievements of Public Works in Italian Eritrea

(Rome) Il Giornale d'Italia published a report by the Italian High Commissioner for East Africa, De Bono, on the achievements of various public works projects held in Italian Eritrea in the past six months. According to the report, Massawa Port was the largest and safest port on the Red Sea, but in the past, it could only transport 300 tons of goods per day. Now the port has been expanded and can transport 3,600 tons of goods per day. Warehouses, docks and oil pools have been completed. The train from Massawa Port to Asmara used to run twice a day, but now it has increased to six times. In addition, the road improvement plan has been completed, including the repair of 109 kilometers of existing roads and the construction of 306 kilometers of new roads. Furthermore, 15 old wells have been repaired and 62 new wells have been drilled in Eritrea. As for the city of Asmara, the population was only 4,500 in the past, but now it has increased to 55,000. A water supply pipe is being built there, which can supply 375 gallons of drinking water per day after completion. The existing hospital in the territory has been expanded and telephones have also been installed. (Havas, 13th)

The authorities in Italian Tripoli in Alexandria have already formed several labor teams and transported them to Eritrea to serve. These workers are mostly recruited from eastern Tripoli. Traffic between Egypt and Tripoli has been completely stopped because of this, because the Arabs are deeply afraid that they will be forced to serve after crossing the border. The people's pro-Abyssinian spirit can be seen from the welcome received by the Egyptian Abyssinian consulate. It is said that the consulate will soon be upgraded to a embassy. Under the strong cooperation of the three departments of the Ministry of the Army, the General Staff Headquarters, and the Inspectorate General of Military Education, the three major departments of military administration, military command, and education will be implemented step by step, in order to establish control within the army. Minister of the Army Hayashi is not light-hearted about this matter. Regardless of the world's evaluation, he will implement what he believes in and dedicate himself to the country. Other chiefs and seniors also have the same feeling. Therefore, Minister of the Army Hayashi will never speak of his advance or retreat at the Three Chiefs Conference. (Den-tsu News Agency, 14th)

(Tokyo) Minister of the Army Hayashi invited Chief of Staff Prince Kan'in to the Minister's residence at 1:30 PM on the 14th and asked Inspector General of Military Education General Watanabe to come to the residence to hold a Three Chiefs Conference. Minister of the Army Hayashi first reported the true details of the Nagata Military Affairs Bureau Director assassination incident in great detail. Next, he expressed the necessity of maintaining strict military discipline and shared his belief in controlling the military. The Chief of Staff and the Inspector General of Military Education both expressed their agreement. As a result, the three decided on the following fundamental policies with a cautious attitude, and the meeting ended at around 2:00 PM. (1) In order to boost the morale of the national army and maintain strict discipline, soldiers are not allowed to act rashly. The national army should be controlled with a solemn attitude to give full play to its true nature. (2) The three chiefs will issue instructions to all their subordinate troops to strictly abide by military discipline in order to thoroughly implement the control work. (Domei News Agency, 14th)

(Tokyo) As a result of the Army's Three Chiefs Conference, important instructions will be issued to the entire army as soon as possible. In order to thoroughly rectify military discipline and control the army, the Minister of the Army will soon convene a division commander's conference or a chiefs of staff conference or a group commander's conference. (Domei News Agency, 14th)

(Tokyo) Minister of the Army Hayashi is running around day and night, trying to clean up the situation and control the military. The Army's leaders and the government are also doing their best to help the Minister of the Army to achieve the great goal of controlling the national army. However, the Minister of the Army himself believes that this incident has a serious nature unprecedented since the founding of the country. When the Inspector General of Military Education was replaced a few days ago, the Army's interior was greatly shocked, and the incident occurred immediately afterwards, so it seems that he has a firm intention to resign. The Minister of the Army is carrying out the policy of controlling the military with the help of the government and the Army's leaders, and after everything is settled, he will resign to take responsibility according to his decision. (Domei News Agency, 14th)

(Tokyo) The Japan Times said that foreign observers believe that the infighting within the Japanese Army is a struggle for power between conservatives and radicals. This is a fundamental mistake. Nagata was a confidant of Minister of the Army Hayashi and strongly supported Minister of the Army Hayashi's policy of prohibiting the Army from interfering in politics. This policy has aroused strong resistance from some members of the Army, who believe that the current domestic and international situation urgently requires the Army to have greater activity and participation in national affairs. The Minister of the Army has decided to maintain the Army as only a strong fighting force without interfering in foreign affairs, believing that the political activities of soldiers are enough to deviate from public opinion and create factions among soldiers. (Reuters, 14th)

The Criminal's Preliminary Trial is Expected to Last Two Months, with a Verdict Possible Within the Year

(Tokyo) Lieutenant Colonel Aizawa, the perpetrator of the assassination of former Army Affairs Bureau Chief Nagata, has had his general situation investigated by the Tokyo Military Police. He has been detained in the First Division Garrison Prison and assigned to the First Division Military Tribunal. The relevant officials have appointed Shimada Tomisaburo, the director of military affairs for the First Division, as the prosecutor, and Okada Tomoichi, the legal officer of the First Division, as the preliminary judge. After passing through Prosecutor Uda's hands, the case will then be transferred to the preliminary hearing. After an investigation by Preliminary Judge Noda, the defendant will be handed back to the prosecutor with a written opinion attached, and submitted to the division commander for formal indictment proceedings to begin the military tribunal process. However, given the nature of the incident, the officials in charge are expediting the investigation, aiming to complete the handling within about two months. Therefore, the preliminary hearing decision may be expedited, and a verdict may be announced within the year. (14th, Jiji News Agency dispatch)

Maintaining Global Silver Prices: The United States Purchases Silver in Large Quantities, Averaging Two Million Ounces Daily, Causing Unease in the London Market

(London) According to well-informed sources here today, the United States is purchasing as much as two million ounces of silver daily to maintain global silver prices. Previously, it had already made two large-scale purchases to prevent a sharp fall in northern silver prices, with one purchase amounting to as much as 50 million ounces. (13th, Guomin News Agency dispatch)

(New York) It is reported that the US Treasury Department purchased approximately 320,000 ounces of silver in New York today at a price of 67.62 cents, followed by 250,000 ounces at 67.12 cents. It is noted that the previous purchase price of large foreign bars was 68 cents. Some observers suggest that speculators anticipated that the US Treasury Department would soon raise silver prices, thus creating a position of great power. The Treasury Department, aware of this, is unwilling to provide further support at its previously fixed price, aiming to eliminate speculators while continuing to purchase silver at lower prices. (13th, Reuters dispatch)

(New York) The New York commercial circles have learned that the US Treasury Department has now ceased silver purchases in foreign markets. It is rumored that Washington intends to abolish the silver purchase program established under the 1934 Silver Purchase Act. This news is considered credible by New York banking circles. It is also said that the government does not plan to abolish the Silver Purchase Act during this congressional term, but will merely quietly terminate its silver purchase program. As for the obligation to purchase silver to establish a gold-silver ratio of four to one, this will be deferred to the future. (14th, Reuters dispatch)

(Washington) The Treasury Department estimated today that the government has profited $216,567,067 since implementing the silver purchase plan. The source of this huge profit is due to purchasing silver at market prices and minting it at a price of $1.29 per ounce. It is claimed that $147,299,823 of the profit was derived from purchasing silver in the global market, and the remainder from domestic silver production. In total, the United States' minting profits have reached $60 million. Comparing this figure with the profits from the silver purchase plan illustrates the extent of the Treasury Department's recent activities. (13th, Guomin News Agency dispatch)

(Washington) Senator Thomas, the leader of the silver advocates, attributed the low silver prices to the Treasury Department's cessation of silver purchases. Even the Treasury Department purchasing at low prices does not reflect the intent of the Silver Purchase Act. Thomas stated, "If silver is purchased and then stored away, it is meaningless. What we need is for the price of silver to rise. If China's currency were linked to the British pound, we could benefit greatly, as we are the country with the largest gold reserves. This is certainly not something I would oppose." (13th, Guomin News Agency dispatch)

(London) The Daily Telegraph, the News Chronicle, the Daily Mail, and the Financial News have all published articles commenting on the fall in silver prices. The Financial News stated, "The American authorities have indicated that they are not prepared to permanently maintain silver prices at a certain level. Therefore, speculators are unloading their inventories in a rush. Consequently, silver merchants generally express some degree of unease regarding the status of silver." (14th, Havas dispatch)

(London) Financial reporters hold differing opinions regarding the future trend of silver. The Times states that while long positions have greatly decreased, they are still not small. If the US authorities feel that they will not be forced to absorb a large amount of silver, they may change their policy of suppressing silver prices. The Financial Times reports that speculators may rush to sell the silver they have purchased in the coming days. If this happens, the US Treasury Department's active assistance will be the only way to avoid a complete collapse of the silver market. The Exchange Telegraph reports that US officials absorbed between 11 million and 12 million ounces of silver yesterday. It is estimated that the United States has purchased approximately 200 million ounces of silver in the London market in the past two months. The positions of long-term speculators have almost completely been liquidated. Now that the silver market has been cleared, a rebound in silver prices is expected. The Daily Telegraph claims that the fortunes of American silver rise and fall with political forces. President Roosevelt is now in a dilemma. He does not want to pay unnecessarily high prices for silver, but he also knows that if he does not purchase in large quantities, the silver market will be chaotic. Therefore, he is solving this problem by gradually lowering the purchase price. Speculators are benefiting from this. It is difficult to predict the ultimate outcome. The East still holds a large amount of silver, and it remains to be seen whether or not it will be sold. Future events depend on the inscrutable actions of the East and the inscrutable policies of President Roosevelt. Who can predict them? (14th, Reuters dispatch)

International Commercial Telegram – Reuters Special Commercial News Telegram, August 14th –

Gold and Silver: The London silver market opened quietly, but there were large-scale sell-offs later, causing prices to plummet. Spot and forward prices both fell by .75, to 29 1/875 pence. India and China sold off in large quantities, while the United States purchased. The market closed stably.

English Gold: The London gold price this morning was 140 shillings and 1 pence, down 2.5 pence.

American Silver: Montreux silver futures opened lower by over 100 points this morning due to sharp declines in London and Bombay silver prices, coupled with uncertainty in American policy.

Exchange Rates: British-American exchange rates opened stable in the London foreign exchange market this morning. The opening rate for British-American exchange was $4.978125, down .0625 from the American-British closing rate yesterday. It rose by .125 within the first hour, to $4.980625, and remained unchanged thereafter.

British-French: British-French exchange rates were adjusted by the equalization authorities this morning. The opening price was 75 francs .01, up 1 pound. It rose by 3 pounds within the first hour, but all the gains made before 1:00 PM were lost, returning to the opening price of 75 francs .01 and remaining unchanged for a time.

Cotton and Wheat: American Cotton: New York cotton market opened lower by several points due to the drop in Liverpool prices. Although prices remained stable after the opening, the cotton market showed a downward trend due to continued favorable crop reports and rumors that President Roosevelt and Secretary of Agriculture Wallace were rejecting cotton loans. However, according to some sources, the cotton market was oversold.

English Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market continued to ease slightly. At 1:00 PM, the October contract price was 5.90, down 3 points.

English Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was slightly more stable today. At 1:00 PM, the October contract price was 5 shillings, 1 penny, and .375, up .25 from yesterday's close.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened higher due to good news from Liverpool and a firming foundation. The same was true for miscellaneous grains.

Rubber: The London rubber market was sluggish this morning. At noon, the transaction price for the October-December contract was 5.8125 pence, the same as yesterday's closing price.

New York: Although there are hopes that market prices will increase, the New York rubber market opened quietly today. Prices fell.

Securities: New York stock market prices fluctuated this morning. Merchants continue to adopt a more cautious attitude. Various prices are still stable, similar to yesterday's closing prices. Sentiment is still good. Silver mining stocks showed a slight decline. General Motors shares fell slightly due to continued profit-taking, but they anticipate a decrease in demand in the fall. Railroad and utility stocks were firm, rising in line with the trend. Oil and steel stocks were stable. The Dow Jones 30 Industrial Average was 128.09, the same as yesterday's closing price. Tao Shangming's Detention: The Japanese Side Believes Tao is Related to the Liu Zuozhou Case; Rescue Efforts are Underway, but the Japanese Have Agreed to Release Him, but Have Not Yet Done So

Beiping correspondence: Tao Shangming, the former Administrative Commissioner of the Aoyu District, was transferred to serve as a counselor in the Political Readjustment Committee. He handed over his duties in Tangshan and came to Beiping to take up his new post. Coincidentally, the Liu Zuozhou assassination case occurred, and the Japanese side suspected that Tao was related to the case. At 3:00 PM on the 5th, he was detained by the Japanese Embassy and has not been released since. Since this event occurred, the outside world has been quite unclear about the true situation. The details of the events are briefly described as follows. Tao is fluent in Japanese and has served as a negotiator in Fengtian, handling diplomatic relations with Japan. During his tenure as Administrative Commissioner in the Luanyu District, he assumed some of the responsibilities of coordination and had many contacts with Japanese personnel. This time, Tao returned to Beiping on the third night after handing over his duties as Commissioner, and the Liu Zuozhou assassination case in Luanzhou happened to occur on the 4th, which was a coincidence. Unexpectedly, it greatly aroused the suspicion of the Japanese side. After Tao returned to Beiping, the next day was a Sunday. At 8:00 AM on the 5th, Tao went to the Political Readjustment Committee to meet with Acting Chairman Wang Kemin to report on the handover process. He then took up the position of counselor. When Liu Zuozhou was assassinated, Japanese military police officer Uemura was wounded by a stray bullet, which greatly dissatisfied the Japanese side. At 11:50 AM on the 5th, Sakai, Chief of Staff of the Tianjin Garrison, and Iga, head of the Yuguan Special Service Agency, came to Beiping from Tianjin. At 2:00 PM, they went to the Diplomatic Building to meet with Acting Chairman Wang to raise serious questions about the Liu case. They left at 3:00 PM and returned to the Japanese Embassy. Believing that Tao was heavily suspected of being involved in the case, they discussed in the military attache's office and decided to invite Tao to the embassy. At 3:30 PM, Banhon contacted Tao by phone, asking Tao to come to the embassy immediately to discuss matters. Tao was meeting guests at his private residence at the time. After receiving the phone call, he went with his follower, Mr. Liu. After a 20 minute meeting, the Japanese side stated that Tao was related to the Liu case. Despite Tao's best efforts to defend himself, it was ineffective, and he was detained in the military attache's office. After the Japanese subjected Tao's follower and car driver to detailed searches, they were released. Tao's family was very anxious upon hearing the news. His wife went to the Political Readjustment Committee to report the situation and asked for help with the rescue. The Political Readjustment Committee considered the matter to be of great importance, so it sent personnel to contact the Japanese side on the one hand, and telegraphed the central government on the other hand to report the situation and request instructions. Tao's paternal uncle and his younger brother, Shangyu, also came to Beiping one after another to coordinate with all parties to find ways to rescue him. In recent days, Jing Rugeng and others have used their personal relationships to intercede with the Japanese side. The Japanese side has gradually understood and agreed to release him today, but he has not yet been released as of tonight. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has protested to the Japanese side about this matter, but the Japanese side has not yet responded. Tao is being treated quite well in the Japanese Embassy, and Tao's wife also visits the Japanese Embassy from time to time. (August 13th)

Impressions of a Southern Tour

— Special Correspondent Qian Hua

(7) Municipal Construction in Guangzhou

The total population of Guangzhou is 1,122,583, of which 635,403 are men and 487,180 are women. In terms of education, there are 33 kindergartens, 185 elementary schools, 7 middle schools, and 15 vocational and specialized schools. As for major municipal construction projects, they include: (1) The electric company is about to be taken over for municipal operation; (2) a Guangzhou Municipal Design Committee is formed, and experts are selected to specialize in design; (3) the construction of the Haizhu Iron Bridge is completed, connecting business north and south of the Pearl River; (4) the Henan embankment is constructed; (5) 18 city parks and 28 city markets are designated and built throughout the city; (6) automatic telephone sets are purchased and suburban residential areas are expanded; (7) the Changdi wharf is reconstructed and the Haizhu Reef is blasted away; (8) a meteorological station is built and a

Page 11

wireless broadcasting station is organized; (9) the Zhongshan Library and the People's Education Center are constructed; (10) the living conditions of rickshaw pullers are improved, and relief centers are established. In terms of municipal finance, there has been a surplus every year since 1930. In 1931, the income was 7,968,389 yuan and the expenditure was 7,682,525 yuan. In 1932, the income was 8,013,7780 yuan and the expenditure was 7,659,349 yuan. In 1933, the income was 7,917,808 yuan and the expenditure was 6,605,905 yuan.

(8) Tea Rooms in Guangzhou's Culinary Scene

Eating in Guangzhou is truly world-renowned. From snacks costing five cents to a dime, to grand meals costing hundreds of yuan per table, almost every building is a place to eat. Even street vendors are constantly shouting to sell food. The most common and affordable places are tea rooms. Besides enjoying tea, one can freely have a snack. The taste is delicious and the prices are fair. People in Guangzhou spend one or two hours, or even six or seven hours, in tea rooms every day. Meeting friends, chatting, eating, and drinking tea all take place there. The business of tea rooms is booming, but in the midst of the worldwide economic crisis, Guangzhou is no exception. Recently, all stores have been offering major discounts, and hotels are cutting prices by 50% or 60%. Even the grand restaurants are loudly offering wholesale prices for entire tables of food. Therefore, the superficially strong Guangzhou market is indeed difficult to maintain. The tea room business has also been affected. Even those who love to eat are starting to think twice and eat at home. Recently, tea room owners, as if in a league, have been hiring female hostesses to attract customers, which has managed to restore some business. Grand restaurants, on the other hand, are using mahjong to attract customers. In the middle of the night, the sound of shuffling tiles can be clearly heard on the streets. Grand hotels are using cigarettes and tobacco to entice customers. Each has its own way of attracting customers. The reporter stayed in Guangzhou for three days and took a public bus once. The bus was small and crowded, and armed personnel had to get on the bus to patrol at any time, which felt very uncomfortable. The horn of the public bus can be stretched to a minute, like the whistle of a ship entering the port, which can startle people from their sleep. In the Shanghai concessions, the crackdown on cars honking their horns for no reason is very strict, and the law is enforced like a mountain, which is indeed much cleaner. The Guangzhou municipal authorities should pay special attention to this point.

Guangzhou Pearl River Vessels

(9) The Situation of the Guangsan Railway

The reporter stayed in Guangzhou for three days. Although the weather was only in the nineties, it was sultry and hot from morning to night, and it was impossible to sleep peacefully all night, which was very painful. On the 5th, I left Guangzhou for Wuzhou. I had previously gone to the Guangzhou office of the Fourth Group Army to inquire about how to get to Wuzhou. The staff was very kind and spoke the Guilin dialect, which was almost the same as Mandarin. They said: First, you can take a small ferry directly from here to Wuzhou, but the ferry is small and crowded, and there is only one ferry every five days, which takes two nights to arrive, and is not comfortable and economical. Second, you can cross the river from here, take the Guangsan train from Shweitang to Sanshui, and then transfer to the Hong Kong-Wuzhou steamer to Wuzhou, which arrives the next day and is more convenient. Therefore, the reporter bought a train ticket to Sanshui from the China Travel Service, and asked for a copy of the departure schedule of the ferry across the river and the train schedule, stating that the ferry would depart from Xihoukou at 10:40 a.m., and the train would depart from Shweitang at 11:10 a.m. The reporter arrived at the ferry dock at 10:10 a.m. and boarded the ferry at 10:20 a.m. Unexpectedly, it did not depart until 11:30 a.m. When asked, the person in charge said that the time here is often changed, and the printed schedule cannot be taken as accurate. This is one thing. After crossing the river, the train departed at 12:10 p.m. There was no ticket inspector on the platform, and no formal red-hatted porter. Passengers crowded in with the old and the young, and the principle of equality was implemented. Those who bought third-class tickets occupied the first and second-class carriages, and the armed comrades were even more impolite, lying down on the first-class seats until the train arrived at Sanshui, when they yawned and got up. This is another thing. A certain employee in uniform on the train took a young lady and sat in the first-class carriage. When the ticket inspector came, they nodded to each other, and the ticket was not checked. They got off the train halfway without paying a penny. This is another thing. It is said that among the railways in Guangdong, the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway, which is jointly run by China and the United Kingdom, is the best. The southern section of the Yuehan Railway and the Guangsan Railway are inferior, and the Chaoshan Railway is even worse. The Guangsan Railway once had a prosperous business, but this year it has been affected by the rural depression, and its business has plummeted. Moreover, due to too many employees and heavy expenses, it loses more than ten thousand yuan a month, resulting in a lifeless state. The floods along the Guangsan Railway are also extremely serious, with vast expanses of water or only the roofs of houses exposed, which is extremely miserable.

(10) The Scenery of the West River and the Huabiao Stone

When exiting Sanshui Station, dozens of boatmen solicit business, shouting and scrambling as if they were going to devour the passengers alive. Two or three policemen drove them away with sticks, but they scattered and gathered again, and the chaos reached its peak. It is urgent to find a way to reform this situation. Along the way, there were also advertising signs for the Hong Kong-Wuzhou steamer, shouting loudly. After walking hundreds of steps, I hired a small boat and zigzagged to board the Guangying, a steamer operating between Hong Kong and Wuzhou. The steamer was extremely clean, about a thousand tons. Standing on the deck and looking at the scenery, the river breeze brushed my face, and I felt refreshed. The steamer set sail at 5:00 p.m., sailing up the West River. The mountains were stacked on top of each other, and the river flowed tortuously. The steamer sailed along the foot of the mountains, with wisps of smoke rising from the cooking fires, echoes of pastoral songs, and fishing boats swaying, with conical hats and hunched figures, creating a beautiful natural picture that broadened my mind. The scenery of the West River is similar to that of the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, with solemn and dangerous natural barriers. At first glance, it seems that there is no way through, but suddenly there is a way out. In summer, when traveling by boat, the river breeze is gentle, and the heat is completely dispelled, and the beautiful scenery is enough to cast aside endless worries. Of all the trips the reporter took until arriving in Wuzhou, this river trip was the most enjoyable. After a night of restful sleep, I woke up very early in the morning. At about 8:00 a.m., when passing Liujiangkou on the river surface, I suddenly saw a peak protruding, with a huge stone growing out of the top, covering the entire mountain top, like a huge stone tablet standing upright, which can be called a wonder. Looking at it from afar with a telescope, there were three large characters "Huabiao Stone" carved on the back of the stone, each a foot in diameter. When asked, people on the boat said that visitors who climb to the top of the mountain can sit on the huge stone. Many of the strokes of the stone carvings have been peeled off, which must have been after a long period of time. Due to upstream flash floods, the river water has risen sharply, and many low-lying areas in the cities along the river have been submerged. The steamer arrived in Wuzhou at 2:00 p.m. The reception staff and police officers boarded the steamer to welcome us, and we took a small boat to Guangxi University to rest. The annual meeting members were staying there.

(11) Labor and Women's Occupations

The liveliness, bravery, and physical strength of women in Guangdong and Guangxi are far beyond the reach of the delicate and frail women of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. When I arrived in Guangzhou, the labor force on the streets was almost equally divided between men and women. Women are engaged in various occupations. Going upstream along the river to Wuzhou, the proportion of women participating in activities gradually increased. Almost all of the baggage carriers at the Sanshui Station were women, ranging in age from twelve or thirteen to forty or fifty. Most of them wore black silk shirts and pants, and were barefoot, with large straw hats, as if they were in uniform. They carried shoulder poles and could carry objects weighing hundreds of pounds. When the reporter got off the train, a young working girl very enthusiastically took my luggage and walked as fast as the wind. I was very ashamed and struggled to keep up behind her with my hands empty. On many small boats, there were also women, either mothers and daughters or mothers-in-law and daughters-in-law, helping to row the oars. Although the reporter and they were separated by language, they never cheated. The small boat approached the large steamer, and the current was turbulent. They skillfully pulled the rope and securely docked the boat. Then, they helped the passengers take their luggage into the cabin. Giving them a penny or two for wine money made them very satisfied and they thanked me repeatedly. When the steamer stopped along the way, there were many women boaters rowing small boats full of fruits, tobacco, and various daily necessities, approaching the side of the steamer and shouting loudly to sell their goods. Their voices were clear and exciting. There was another kind of touching sound wave. There were even more working women in Wuzhou City. They could do anything that men could do. They were also active outside, earning money, and equally sharing the various rights and obligations of the family, truly achieving equal work for men and women. Once, the reporter hired a small boat to tour the river. The boat was manned by a middle-aged couple and a child who was less than one year old. Sometimes the child fell asleep and was placed under the deck. When he woke up and cried, the wife would row the oars while using her feet to rock the child's body. Sometimes she would carry the child on her back in a cloth bag, which did not hinder any work. However, women's education is too poor. Most of the working women are illiterate. Perhaps those who have received education are unwilling to work so hard.

(12) Touring Wuzhou

Wuzhou is the commercial center of Guangxi, with prosperous streets and magnificent buildings. However, due to recent flash floods and rising river waters, many low-lying streets have been submerged. In addition, the rural areas are depressed, and the market is in an extremely sluggish state. According to people in the shops, the business this year is only about two-thirds of last year's. There are cars and rickshaws in the city, but they are rarely seen. Most people walk. Wuzhou is surrounded by mountains, and many streets are built on mountain slopes. The river flows through the city, and the scenery is very beautiful. There is a tung oil factory, a pharmaceutical factory, a waterworks, and a sulfuric acid factory jointly run by Guangdong and Guangxi. On the afternoon of the 7th, more than 200 annual meeting members arrived one after another, and were accompanied by receptionists to tour the city and visit the various factories. The tung oil factory is relatively well-developed, with a capital of 100,000 yuan. Preparations began in September last year, and work began on May 1st this year. Guangxi's annual output of tung oil is more than 200,000 dan, most of which has not been refined and has poor composition. When exported in Hong Kong, it is difficult to sell at a good price. Therefore, the provincial authorities are striving to rectify the situation. The purpose of running this factory is to inspect the quality of tung oil and to refine impurities. It is stipulated that oil merchants must send their oil to the factory for inspection or refining before exporting. The refining fee is 6 jiao and 5 fen per city dan. At the time, the merchants were quite worried. In May, when the factory first opened, the business was very slow. In June, those requesting refining reached more than 4,000 dan, and those requesting inspection reached more than 3,000 dan. In July, it increased to more than 16,000 dan. The trend of continued growth this month still continues. Normally, it can only be sold for more than 30 yuan per dan in Hong Kong. After refining, the selling price increases, so merchants are happy to send it for refining. It is truly a beneficial business that achieves two goals at once. The manager is Guo Canglong, the technician is Wen Xiangxing, and the technicians are Xu Wenbin and Jia Weiting. There are more than 20 workers. Next, we visited the pharmaceutical factory, which is divided into a chemical analysis department and a pharmaceutical manufacturing department. It also opened on January 1st this year, and the order is well-organized and full of spirit. The sulfuric acid factory was originally jointly run by Guangdong and Guangxi. The sales of sulfuric acid in Guangxi were very sluggish, and it is now in a state of shutdown. The factory's capital reached more than 800,000 yuan, all of which has been lost, and only the machinery remains to generate income.

Women Boaters Active on the Wuzhou River

Scenery of the Sanshui Wharf

(13) The Current Situation of Guangxi University

Guangxi University is the only university in Guangxi Province. It is built on Butterfly Mountain in Wuzhou, with beautiful scenery. The annual meeting members are all lodged there. It takes about half a mile to walk from the gate to the dormitory, and the dining hall is on the top of the mountain, which takes another half a mile. This is to train students to run. The campus covers an area of about a thousand acres, surrounded by mountains. There are 21 buildings, including classrooms, dormitories, libraries, and auditoriums. The regular expenses are more than 20,000 yuan per month, which are remitted on time without delay. There are currently more than 300 undergraduate students and more than 400 high school students. The undergraduates are co-educational, but the high school is not. The undergraduates are divided into five departments: agriculture, forestry, mining, engineering, and science. The president is Ma Junwu, and the vice president is Pan Zhuqi. The school pays special attention to military training, and the students are exceptionally simple and hardworking. There are many students who stay on campus during the summer to work and tutor. The students can take on extremely hard work, such as carrying earth, washing clothes, and doing carpentry. The school subsidizes them with more than ten yuan per month, which is not like the university students in other cities who can only live a comfortable life. Most of the students' uniforms are made of locally produced gray cloth, and all have shaved heads. When on campus, they get up at 4:30 in the morning and start military training. Each quarter, each class can select two outstanding students who are completely exempt from tuition fees. Although the university is co-educational, the boundaries are very strict. This year is the first class to graduate, all in science. There are 31 graduates, 8 of whom are retained to work at the school, and the rest are all going to Nanning. The provincial government has agreed to assign them jobs, which can avoid the pain of unemployment upon graduation. At 7:30 p.m. on the 7th, Guangxi University President Ma Junwu and Vice President Pan Zhuqi held a welcome meeting for the annual meeting members in the auditorium. Ma Jun gave a speech, which was extremely humble, saying that he hoped for guidance in everything. The accommodation and meals in the dormitory were very cordial, but the order was slightly chaotic due to the large number of people, which was also unavoidable. They are now departing for Nanning in two batches. The reporter departed with the first batch at 9:00 p.m. on the 8th. That evening at 6:00 p.m., President Ma Junwu and Wuzhou Public Security Bureau Chief Hao Huan hosted a banquet for everyone at the Dongtian Restaurant. After the meal, they boarded the steamer and are expected to arrive around the 11th. (Sent from Wuzhou on the 8th)

Songjiang: Pregnant Woman Drowns After Losing Footing While Washing Clothes

Zhao, the daughter-in-law of Wang Xuetang, a resident of Xima Bridge, Fenglezhen in this city, was 28 years old. Her husband, Runhe, worked as a clerk at the Xinhe Pawnshop in Zhujing. Since their marriage, they had had one son and one daughter, but the son died young. She was recently pregnant again, already six months along, and with a large belly. Everyone said she had the look of bearing a son, to fulfill the Wang family's hopes. However, the pregnant woman went to the riverside to wash clothes at about 1:00 p.m. today and did not return home for a long time. Her family went to look for her and only saw her clothes on the riverside. Knowing that something bad had happened, they searched for her body. It was not until about 6:00 p.m. that a cargo boat found her body in the same place. It is now being kept at the public cemetery so that her family can return to Songjiang with a coffin.

Wuxi: Appeal to Exempt Wheat Bran from Taxes

The Oil Mill Industry Association of this county recently received a letter from its members Hengde Oil Mill and Runfengchang Oil Mill stating that Guangzhou tax merchants are planning to levy a surcharge of 25 cents per picul on wheat bran transported from anywhere. However, this wheat bran is made from soybeans, which is a domestic fertilizer essential for farmland in rural areas. The Ministry of Finance and the Southwest Political Committee have issued announcements that domestic sales are tax-exempt. Now, the Guangdong Provincial Government has abolished 42 kinds of arbitrary taxes and levies, but the tax merchants are blinded by greed and disregard the burden on merchants and the public. If the levy is implemented, it will not only promote the sales of imported fertilizers and put domestic industry and commerce in a desperate situation, but also completely violate the government's repeated orders to maintain the domestic product case. After receiving the letter, the association yesterday forwarded it to the county chamber of commerce, requesting it to telegraph the Guangdong authorities and make every effort to stop it, and also telegraphed the Guangzhou City Chamber of Commerce to strive for it together in order to protect domestic products.

Wife and Concubine Quarrel Leads to Murder

Wang Gengquan, a 30-year-old resident of Wangjiali Lane, Xinan Township, Beiqiao, Third District, was a coppersmith foreman at the Sixth Japanese Cotton Mill on Xiaoshadu in Shanghai, earning a good income. His wife, Zhu, had given birth to two sons and one daughter. However, Wang was lustful. In November of last year, he became involved with a female worker named Zhang at the same factory and took her as his concubine. Unfortunately, this did not last long. Gengquan was dismissed by the factory for poor work. In June of this year, he took Zhang home, causing frequent quarrels between his wife and concubine. The day before yesterday evening, the first wife had another argument with Zhang. In a fit of anger, Zhang committed suicide by hanging herself that night. Later, her husband discovered it, but she had already died and could not be revived. The next day, Qian Yaoqing, the head of the Nian Liu Wu Tu, reported the case to the prosecutor's office, requesting an autopsy. Prosecutor Shen led a forensic examiner Wang and bailiffs to the countryside to perform an autopsy, which confirmed that she had died by suicide by hanging. After the autopsy, he ordered the family to prepare a coffin for burial and await further investigation.

Hangzhou: Police Officer Indicted for Accidental Shooting Death

The case of Ruan Hongkui, a police officer from the Fifth Precinct of the Hangzhou Municipal Public Security Bureau, accidentally shooting and killing Lu Meihong, an employee of the Huajinli Clock and Watch Inlay Shop, has been prosecuted. Initially, the Public Security Bureau only transferred the suspected apprentice Zhou Shanqing to the court, while the police officer who caused the accident was retained by the bureau, causing public outrage in the area. Local gentry Yang Yaowen and Ling Shuixin, along with 33 shops in Nanxingqiao, jointly published a newspaper, raising six questions to the bureau, accusing it of protecting the police and perverting the law. The Hangzhou Court specially dispatched Prosecutor Chen Huaming to investigate. He determined that Lu Meihong died from a bullet entering her head and that the claim of wiping the gun was also a light way to state the facts. He prosecuted the case as one of causing death by negligence. The suspected apprentice Zhou Shanqing was released as he had no involvement.

Correspondence

Letter from Tang Zhigao

I have read the letter from Zhou Xuewen et al. in Shen Bao on the 3rd of this month, refuting my letter of July 27th requesting a correction. They stated that the Nijiatan is a local public property, and its ownership belongs to the local public, not to the Jiazi Disaster Memorial Association, etc. I believe that the official certificate serves as proof of property rights. Since the Memorial Association holds the official certificate, the ownership of the land naturally belongs to the Memorial Association. The original letter stated that there were two official certificates, and that the Zhang Shude household was redeemed through donations from local citizens such as Zheng Bocang, and not redeemed by the Jiazi Disaster Memorial Association. How could it be falsely claimed as belonging to the Memorial Association? The Memorial Association is essentially an empty shell, and everything relies on its members. Zheng Bocang and others were the initiators of the Memorial Association, and there is documented proof of this. Yet, they are being referred to as non-members, which is utterly ridiculous. The original letter stated that since the Nijiatan is a public property where permanent occupation is forbidden, and not a private property of the Jiazi Disaster Memorial Association, Tang Zhigao, Yin Shisheng, and a few other individuals cannot use the Memorial Association's name to dispose of the altar. Since the construction of the memorial pavilion at the Nijiatan, it has been registered and approved, and it is not a private property. We, who manage the association affairs, are impartial and selfless. If it is said that a few individuals cannot dispose of the altar, then who is in charge of the Memorial Association? The original letter stated that the excavated remains have been collected into thirty-one wooden boxes, and it was publicly agreed to seal them up and bury them on a selected date. Why were they secretly buried by hired laborers in the dead of night before the due date? This time, after the prosecutor arrived at the tomb to excavate and examine, why did the location not match the indicated location? Why were there missing boxes? Why were some seals present and some absent? Why were the remains in the boxes in different states of dryness and moisture? And why was there an empty box? When constructing houses and renovating the pavilion at the Nijiatan, the discovery of remains naturally led to their burial. Why is anyone else's advice needed? The prosecutor only verified thirty boxes at the altar, which is certainly not incorrect. As for the presence or absence of seals, it has been more than three months since the burial, and they would naturally have decayed. Regarding the different states of dryness and moisture of the remains, if it is said that the dry ones were the original bones, then where did the moist ones come from? If it is said that the moist ones were the original bones, then where did the dry ones come from? It should be known that the soil has varying degrees of dryness, and therefore the remains have varying degrees of dryness and moisture. The principle is very clear. As for the empty box, the workers buried it simply because they saw a box; there was no other intention. If it is said that it was intentionally discarded, what use would dry bones be? The various criticisms in that letter are excessively troublesome. The original letter stated that the six hundred and twenty-one yuan from Pastor Bu was his congratulatory gift at the time. Pastor Bu intended to donate it to the orphanage as an education fund. Tang Zhigao violated his intention and had someone find a way to take it back for the purpose of dismantling the pavilion and destroying the tomb. Pastor Bu still speaks of it with heartache. This is nothing short of slander. According to that letter, everything stated is the opposite of the truth. See the Shen Bao of the 7th; Pastor Bu has already issued a special letter clarifying it. The original letter stated that forty-eight wounded soldiers were buried in the sixteenth year. The roster of wounded soldiers at the Fifth Convalescent Hospital clearly records the month, day, and location of their deaths and burials, and it has been reported to the General Headquarters of the Chinese Red Cross Society, with records available. At that time, wounded soldiers from various locations were mostly buried on the spot. The construction of the memorial pavilion was completed in the sixteenth year of the Republic. In that year, not a single coffin was buried at the altar. We personally witnessed it, so this can be called blatant lying. Recalling that in March and April of this year, Zhou Xuewen and others filed lawsuits one after another, and also published in various newspapers, saying that unscrupulous gentry stole and sold the Nijiatan, and at the same time, demolished Pastor Bu's memorial pavilion and exhumed the remains. I considered it worthless and did not argue with them, knowing that the truth would eventually come to light. In the future, if any such writing is discovered again, I implore the public to discern it clearly and not waste any more breath. Initiated by Tang Zhigao, representative of the Songjiang Jiazi Disaster Memorial Association, 24, 8, 10.

Mayor Wu and Others Negotiate for Emergency Flood Relief Loans; China, Communications, and Three Banks Advance 300,000 Yuan; Other Banks Advance 200,000 Yuan

The Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces held its first joint meeting of directors and supervisors on the 10th. Recognizing the urgent need for relief in the disaster areas, and the need to plan for relief funds, Mayor Wu Tiecheng convened a meeting at Wanglu on Haige Road at 4:30 PM on the afternoon of the 12th. Xu Jingren, Wang Yiting, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Jinglai, Chen Guangfu, Lu Bohong, Lin Kanghou, Zhao Puqing, Yu Zuoting, and others attended the meeting to discuss borrowing 500,000 yuan from banks for emergency relief. During the meeting, it was approved that Mayor Wu, Lu Bohong, Chen Guangfu, and Wang Xiaolai would negotiate separately. It is heard that Mayor Wu has negotiated with the Central, China, and Communications banks for a loan of 300,000 yuan, and the three banks will hold a meeting to allocate the loan amounts. The remaining 200,000 yuan will also be negotiated separately by Lu Bohong and Chen Guangfu. When the Bankers' Association convened a regular meeting the day before yesterday, it specifically brought this matter up for discussion and unanimously approved it. Therefore, yesterday the Bankers' Association specially issued a notice to all member banks, confirming the amount to be held. All banks are accepting these loans as a charitable act. Once confirmed, they will be submitted to the Flood Relief Association for distribution and emergency relief.

Municipal Government Notice: Unify Fundraising Organizations; No Need to Establish Separate Names and Issue Donation Appeals

Wu Tiecheng, Mayor of this city, issued Notice No. 259 yesterday to unify the handling of fundraising for emergency flood relief in various provinces in this city. Since the beginning of summer this year, continuous rain and flooding have caused severe disasters in Hubei, Jiangxi, Shandong, Henan, Hebei, and other provinces, urgently requiring relief. Various charitable organizations and relief agencies in this city have been eagerly calling for help out of benevolence and a desire to provide assistance. However, this matter is significant, and without a unified fundraising organization, it will be difficult to concentrate efforts. All sectors of this city, recognizing this, have already initiated the organization and establishment of the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces to handle fundraising for emergency flood relief in various provinces in a unified manner, in order to seek assistance. In the future, all charitable organizations and relief agencies in this city should participate together to fully assist the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces in urging donations. There is no need to establish separate names and issue donation appeals to avoid fragmentation. All relief funds and relief supplies should be distributed by the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces to concentrate efforts and provide assistance. It is hoped that people at home and abroad will generously donate grain and funds to relieve the disaster victims and mitigate the catastrophe. This notice is hereby issued.

Consulate General in Batavia Reports to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission: Reports of Anti-Chinese Sentiment in the Dutch East Indies Are Completely Inaccurate

In recent years, overseas Chinese have occasionally been subjected to incidents of exclusion due to the impact of the economic crisis. Judging from the recent situation, the status of overseas Chinese seems to be improving day by day, and their situation is also gradually improving. However, a Hong Kong newspaper recently published a news item entitled "Returned Overseas Chinese Describe the Truth of the Dutch East Indies' Abuse of Overseas Chinese," which stated that the government of the Dutch East Indies ordered overseas Chinese to leave the country, prohibited overseas Chinese education, Chinese newspapers, inspected letters, and increased the entry tax to 1,000 guilders. It also stated that the first batch of 240 expelled overseas Chinese arrived in Hong Kong on May 15, and the second batch of overseas Chinese chartered ships to return home. Domestic newspapers also reprinted the report, and people in society were deeply surprised, and those concerned about overseas Chinese affairs were particularly anxious. At that time, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission heard this rumor and, believing that it was strange and absurd, and fearing that the rumor-mongers had ulterior motives, immediately ordered the Consulate General in Batavia to investigate and report the details. Recently, the Consulate General reported that the news report was pure fabrication. The latest news about overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies is summarized as follows: It is true that overseas Chinese residing in the Dutch East Indies have been dismissed, unemployed, or unable to pay taxes due to the impact of the economic downturn in recent years, but the number is small and they were not expelled by the local government. The so-called "wealthy families are given 20 days to return to their country, and the working class is given two weeks to return, otherwise they will be forcibly expelled and their property will be confiscated" is entirely unfounded. The report that newspaper reporters were expelled and returned to their country was also denied by the two newspapers. The Batavia New Daily and the Tian Sheng Daily have also published articles refuting the rumors. The so-called "letters sent to government agencies are confiscated" has been investigated by the local post and telecommunications bureau and the Chinese Affairs Department, and it has been proven to be untrue. Government agencies have been receiving and sending letters to and from the Dutch East Indies as usual for several months without any loss. The so-called increase in special taxes and entry taxes is also entirely false. The entry tax in the Dutch East Indies has been 150 guilders per person since it was increased in 1931, and if there are any future tax increase proposals, our government will certainly argue strongly to abolish them. In terms of education, all Chinese schools in the Dutch East Indies are free to teach Chinese, and Chinese history and geography are also included in the curriculum as usual. However, it is true that students under the age of 18 are not allowed to listen to political speeches. As for the report that students of Jinan University must return to the Dutch East Indies within three years, and will not be allowed to return to the port if they overstay, the Chinese Affairs Department and the Immigration Supervision Department of the Ministry of Justice of the Dutch East Indies have stated that there is no such thing. In summary, all of these points prove that the report in a certain Hong Kong newspaper is divorced from the facts and has no basis. At a time when the country is experiencing many troubles, it is difficult to guarantee that there are no villains who fabricate facts and spread rumors, attempting to provoke discord between China and the Netherlands in order to profit. However, the facts are clear, and if we can discern them, we will not be deceived by them.

Hankou Suddenly Encountered a Hurricane; China National Aviation Corporation Aircraft Destroyed; Shanghai-Hankou Flight as Usual Today

At 6:30 PM on the 13th of this month, Hankou suddenly encountered a hurricane, which was very strong. Two No. 2 and No. 4 Loening aircraft and one Stinson aircraft belonging to the China National Aviation Corporation, which were parked at the Taikoo Wharf riverside seaplane airport in Hankou, had their float chains broken by the wind at the time, causing the No. 2 Loening aircraft to collide with No. 4. There was no time to defend, and the wings of both aircraft were destroyed. The Stinson aircraft was then swept into the huge waves by the hurricane, and the force of the wind at the time can be imagined. After the company received a telegram from the Hankou office reporting the disaster, it immediately reported it to the ministry and formulated follow-up measures. In addition to finding ways to salvage the sunken aircraft and transport the Loening aircraft to Shanghai for repairs, a solution has been determined for air transport between Shanghai and Hankou. Westbound and eastbound flights will continue as usual today.
