Aviation Industry Should Pay Attention; Avoid Flying Low Near the Tianli Liquefied Gas Plant; Light Gas Easily Catches Fire in the Air When Released

According to the Central News Agency, the Tianli Liquefied Gas Products Factory on the north bank of the Suzhou River in this city has been progressing steadily since it started construction, and its work is becoming increasingly intense. Recently, the China Aviation Association received a letter from the factory stating that the company is engaged in the business of manufacturing liquefied gas products using a fixed method of atmospheric liquefaction and has now started work. Although all the light gas generated in the electrolyzers is stored in gas storage tanks, it is sometimes necessary to release the light gas into the air at the beginning of work. This light gas is very easy to catch fire. If aircraft fly at low altitude near the factory, it is possible to cause danger to both parties. In addition to sending special letters to China National Aviation Corporation and Eurasia Aviation Corporation, it is requested that your association send letters to relevant agencies to inform their pilots to avoid flying low near the factory to ensure safety. The factory is located on the north bank of the Suzhou River (opposite Bailinan Road), about one mile from the railway. There are four silver gas storage tanks there, which are very easy to identify. The Aviation Association has distributed the letters accordingly. It is also heard that Tianli Factory mainly produces nitric acid and ammonia. Recently, due to the overproduction of hydrochloric acid at the Tianyuan Electrochemistry Factory under the same system, it has started to manufacture sal ammoniac (used as a raw material for dry batteries, etc., which has never been manufactured domestically) to alleviate the situation and meet the needs of domestic goods factories.

Stamp Tax Law to Be Implemented on Schedule; Chamber of Commerce Issues Special Notice; Tax Law and Implementation Rules Being Printed; Lecture to Be Held on August 24

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce stated that the new Stamp Tax Law has been scheduled to be implemented on September 1. In order to clarify matters for the business community, it has decided to hold a lecture on the 24th of this month to explain the comparison between the old and new tax laws, and will open a special column in the No. 8 Commercial Monthly to explain the details. Special notices have been issued to the four branch offices in Wusong, Jiangwan, Pudong, and Nanshi, as well as to various industry associations: Respectfully, the Stamp Tax Law promulgated in December of last year has been ordered to be implemented on September 1. The Stamp Tax Law Implementation Rules have also been formulated by the Ministry of Finance and will be implemented at the same time. These regulations are necessary tools for merchants to check. This association has already printed 20,000 copies each, but the number of members in each association varies, and it is difficult to predict the exact number to be issued. Each association or branch office should determine the number of members or stores in its area, and how many are needed per industry and per area, and collect and distribute them on their behalf. Each set includes one copy of the Stamp Tax Law and one copy of the Implementation Rules, and a fee of two cents in national currency will be charged for the paper and printing costs, which should be paid along with the collection. This association will distribute them in the order of application. If the 20,000 copies have already been distributed at the time of application, or if there are not many copies remaining, the shortage will be made up when the second batch is printed. In addition, because the Stamp Tax Law and the Provisional Regulations have many differences, there may be confusion about the changes, so a special column has been opened in the 8th issue of the 15th volume of the Commercial Monthly to explain the main points. However, it is feared that the readership of that monthly magazine is not widespread enough, so a meeting has been scheduled for 9:00 AM on Saturday, the 24th of this month, to gather representatives from various industries to explain the purpose in person, so as to prepare before implementation and reduce misunderstandings and penalties after implementation. Corresponding letters have been sent. Please investigate and handle accordingly.

Shanghai's Opium Suppression Problem: Director Cai's Broadcast Speech Yesterday; Anti-Smoking Advocacy Team of the Public Safety Bureau Sets Off This Morning to Promote the Cause

Yesterday (the 14th) at 4:30 PM, Cai Jinjun, Director of the Municipal Public Safety Bureau, gave a speech on the "Opium Suppression Problem in Shanghai" at the Sino-Western Drug Store radio station. He said: (1) Dear compatriots, today I, Jinjun, am honored to be invited by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau to give this radio speech. I feel very honored to have such a good opportunity to speak to all the compatriots in the city. The topic I am speaking on today is "The Opium Suppression Problem in Shanghai." Before discussing opium suppression, we should understand the harms of opium. Facts tell us that a person addicted to opium is physically weak, economically distressed, and morally bankrupt. Because opium contains morphine, a toxic substance, addicts suffer pathological changes in their physiology. Healthy people become sick, mildly ill people become seriously ill, and seriously ill people become incurable. Therefore, smokers are always thin as rails and mentally depressed. At the same time, as everyone knows, people with opium addictions must smoke every day. Therefore, opium becomes an indispensable necessity. Wealthy people increase this burden, and in a few years, their family property is squandered, turning them into beggars. Poor people's lives become even more difficult. When there is no other way, their last resort is to take risks and commit crimes. This is an inevitable phenomenon caused by the increased burden and economic hardship of opium smokers. Furthermore, opium smokers, no matter how knowledgeable or skilled they may be, are unable to engage in productive work due to their physical and mental state. Coupled with the need to spend money on opium, increasing the burden, these two conditions constitute their immoral behavior. They disregard propriety, justice, integrity, and a sense of shame, and they do not know what the law is. I remember that I once interrogated a robber. I asked him why he became a robber. He said, "He was originally a rich man's son and studied at a university for two years. Because of opium smoking, he squandered his family property. Later, relying on the skills he learned at the university, he tried to find a job. However, either his physical and mental strength was insufficient, or people disliked his opium smoking, and he eventually became unemployed. At first, he relied on petty theft to maintain his life. Later, the neighbors found out and took precautions. With no means of livelihood and a hungry stomach, he had no choice but to join a gang of bad people and become a robber." This is a real-life example of the decline of an opium smoker. Also, in the past, the detention center of the Public Safety Bureau had a particularly large number of opium-smoking criminals, which is also clear evidence. From this, we can see that smoking opium is indeed a suicidal and sinful act. Smoking opium is not only a suicidal and sinful act, but also a cause of national decline. Because opium smokers not only poison themselves, but also pass on a weak body, low intelligence, and bad habits to their descendants, trapping them in a situation from which they cannot extricate themselves. Opium smokers are mentally depressed, materially unproductive, and physically weak. Their descendants are not vigorous. Therefore, if a nation has a large proportion of opium smokers, that nation will inevitably decline because it loses its national "strength." Since the Opium War, our nation has been weak and bullied by others. This is the result of the poison of opium. Because the harm opium inflicts on individuals, society, and the nation is so serious, opium suppression is a serious issue. Only opium suppression can reduce social evils, and only opium suppression can revive the Chinese nation. (2) Since the opium suppression problem is so serious, let us now review the achievements of past opium suppression efforts. Since the Opium War, whether under the Manchu Qing government or the Northern Warlord era, opium was banned by law, and opium smoking was a crime punishable by law. However, after many years, many opium offenders have been punished every year, but to this day, there has been no success. Why is this? The reason is that they did not know that the legislation was strict enough, the ban was too short, and the necessary procedures were not taken into account. There were neither strict control measures nor consistent and effective steps, and the general public did not assist the government. Therefore, the problem has continued to worsen day by day and has not yet been eradicated. Our Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has seen through this point, so he has made a great determination to adopt the six-year ban plan decided by the National Assembly in the past, deciding that from this year to the 29th year, as the prohibition period, taking two measures, one is to promote the New Life Movement, to shift the social atmosphere, to encourage the people to assist the government in prohibiting opium, on the one hand, to use scientific methods, with the power of the government, to force smokers to quit. Indeed, the responsibility of society for the ban on opium is greater than the responsibility of the government. Revolution must first reform the heart, political change must first change customs. Changing customs is to shift the atmosphere. To shift the atmosphere, we must rely on the power of society. Although society does not reward opium smokers, it does not punish them either. Opium smokers have been given a kind of forgiveness. Therefore, their numbers have increased considerably day by day. Taking Shanghai as an example, according to the statistics of the Public Safety Bureau on the seizure of opium and potent narcotics, 1,500 offenders were seized in the 21st year, 6,176 offenders were seized in the 22nd year, and 6,956 offenders were seized in the 23rd year. Judging from this, there is no doubt that the number of smokers is increasing year by year. This is clear evidence of the lack of social sanctions. We all know that the custom of foot-binding has a history of seven or eight hundred years, from the Five Dynasties to the present day. Since the founding of the Republic of China, foot-binding has been promoted, and in less than twenty years, the centuries-old custom of foot-binding has been eradicated. Because everyone in society believes that this is the right thing to do, the concept of beauty of small feet has also changed. The general young men will not marry women with bound feet, and the general women with bound feet are in danger of not being able to marry. Therefore, the atmosphere has changed. Women who have already bound their feet immediately unbound them, and women who have not bound their feet dare not bind them anymore. This is the effect of social sanctions. When I was in Jiangxi last year, I went to visit Linchuan County. There is a Pengxi Town Experimental District, which is one of the most vigorous places to promote the New Life Movement, especially for opium suppression. There is a room in the district that is filled with more than a thousand confiscated pipes. It is said that they were voluntarily surrendered by their relatives. The methods they adopted for opium suppression are very clever, organized by the New Life Movement Association. They organized a Women's Life Improvement Association. Banning opium is the most important work of the association. They use the women in the family as supervisors of opium suppression, mothers for sons, wives for husbands, sisters for brothers, etc. If they have an opium addiction, they first persuade them with bitter words. If they cannot be persuaded with words, they follow it with tears. If they cannot be moved by tears, they follow it with estrangement. It should be known that parents, brothers, sisters, and spouses are all kinds of innate feelings. If these feelings are severed, both sides feel pain. Every family is like this, and no one sympathizes with the smoker. Therefore, it is very effective. If they still do not quit, they will implement the second step, that is, the family will sever his economic relations, and relatives and friends will not provide assistance, so that he feels that he has no way to survive without quitting opium. Who does not cherish his reputation, who does not cherish his life? Therefore, in less than a few months in Pengxi Town, all the smokers in the town have completely quit opium under this strict supervision. This is a very good example to learn from. From this, we can know the power of social sanctions. (3) Now let's talk about our Shanghai, the largest city in the country. It has more than three million people. It is the center of China's economy and culture, and it is also a place where Chinese and foreigners live together. The rise and fall of the nation depends on the eyes of both Chinese and foreigners. The urgency of opium suppression is beyond words. Therefore, the Opium Suppression Committee was established on July 1 this year to discuss opium suppression measures and decided to implement them in stages. The first step is to register all smokers. After the registration deadline, we will find out the number of people who smoke opium and the amount of opium paste needed. Based on the statistics, we will limit the number of opium paste stores and gradually reduce them until opium is completely banned. The Public Safety Bureau is ordered to handle the registration of smokers. A public notice was posted on July 22, and at the same time, orders were issued to all sub-bureaus, divisions, and teams to start registering smokers from today. There are already quite a few people who have registered. The purpose of registration is to count the exact number of smokers in order to quit in stages. The registration period is set at six months, from July to the end of September as the automatic registration period. The Bureau organized a persuasion team to persuade smokers to register. From October to the end of December, it is the period of compulsory registration. The Bureau will order the arrested offenders to register. At the same time, the Bureau plans to have three kinds of registration application forms, one is the application form for a general opium quitting license, the second is the application form for a pauper's license, and the third is the application for opium quitting. However, those who apply for a pauper's opium quitting license must submit a letter of guarantee to the Bureau for verification and issuance of a license to prove whether they are paupers. Those who apply to quit opium must also register first in accordance with the regulations and wait to be sent to the opium quitting hospital, and they must also fill out a letter of guarantee guaranteeing that they can be tested at any time after quitting and will never smoke again. In addition, if the smoker travels, he must submit the license he has received to the Bureau for a travel certificate. In short, the procedures should be as simple as possible, and the methods should be as thorough as possible. The Bureau has now established the rules for smokers' registration and the detailed rules for implementing the registration of opium-smoking households within a time limit. All the procedures for application registration, the regulations for penalties, and the handling of opium cases are recorded in it. The police have been sent to distribute them door-to-door. I think everyone has seen them and does not need to explain them in detail. (4) However, opium suppression is a major move to shift the atmosphere and a great plan to revive the nation. Relying on the power of the government alone is not enough. All the smokers in the city must realize it, and all the compatriots in the city must assist us in order to achieve the goal. The reasons for this have been stated before and do not need to be repeated here. Compatriots throughout the city, we must recognize the seriousness of the Shanghai opium suppression problem. We must understand our responsibilities. I hope that the compatriots who are addicted to opium will quickly wake up and come to the Public Safety Bureau to register and ask to quit. I hope that the compatriots who are not addicted to opium will strive to promote the New Life Movement, assist the government in banning opium, and shift the social atmosphere. In particular, I hope that the female compatriots in the city will organize Women's Life Improvement Associations and emulate the methods of Pengxi Town, Linchuan County, Jiangxi, to urge their families to quit opium. I believe that it can be quit within six years. This is the gospel of the citizens and the key to the revival of the nation. (The End)

The Dagong News Agency reported that the Municipal Public Safety Bureau, in accordance with the regulations and bylaws of the time-limited opium suppression promulgated by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's headquarters, is immediately implementing the city's opium suppression movement. The regulations stipulate that the first phase, from July to the end of September of this year, is the deadline for smokers to surrender themselves. The second phase, from October 1 to the end of December, is the deadline for compulsory registration of smokers. After the announcement of the measures, registration will begin immediately. In order to eliminate smokers within a time limit, quit their addiction, and make the public pay attention to the significance of opium suppression, the Municipal Public Safety Bureau has specially ordered all district bureaus and district offices in the city to organize persuasion teams, which have been established. They will set off this morning to take on the work of persuasion and publicity. Song Ziwen, Li Shizeng, and Wang Minyi took the night train from Beijing yesterday and arrived in Shanghai this morning.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Utilizes the Surplus of the Boxer Indemnity to Add Two River Steamers; Plan Already Finalized

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will utilize the surplus from the British Boxer Indemnity to add Yangtze River ships. It is found that the remaining balance of the funds is 40,000 pounds. Using this sum to build a river steamer would only be sufficient for one ship. Now it is learned that the company has decided that in addition to building a river steamer with the remaining funds, another motor engine upper Yangtze River steamer will be added to run the Hankou-Yichang route. However, the surplus of 40,000 pounds is only enough to purchase the materials for two ships. The cost of the hull and construction equipment is still short of 400,000 to 500,000 yuan. It has been decided that the company will raise funds separately.

Revised Ship Design

The design of the new river steamer was originally planned to be built according to the Taikoo Company's Wusong vessel, with a deadweight of 3,426 tons, mainly for cargo loading. The ship is equipped with hooks for loading and unloading large cargo. After several meetings, the previous plan was revised, and it was decided to build it according to the design of the company's Jiang'an and Jiangshun vessels, with a deadweight of 4,327 tons, with both cargo and passenger transportation as the principle. The draft will also be improved so that flood and shallow water can be freely adjusted without hindering navigation. As for the motor boat, it has a deadweight of 500 tons and is mainly used for cargo transportation.

Proceeding with Material Purchases

After several meetings and revisions, the ship design was finalized and submitted to the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board of Directors and reported to the Ministry of Communications for record. The materials used for the two ships are still being purchased in the UK, transported to Shanghai, and then handed over to the Jiangnan Shipyard for construction. The import of materials for the two ships has been approved by the Central Government for tax exemption. All matters have now been completed, and the purchase of materials from England to China will be carried out immediately.

Since August This Year: Rainfall Exceeds Last Year by One-Third; Total of 713 Millimeters Since the Beginning of the Year; Cotton Will Mature Late, but Early and Late Rice Are Not Affected

Since August this year, Shanghai has received one-third more rainfall than last year, resulting in excessive growth of cotton seedlings and late maturity. The details are as follows:

August Rainfall

According to the records of the Xujiahui Observatory, from January 1 to August 13 this year, Shanghai has received 713.6 millimeters of rainfall, equivalent to 28.09 inches. The rainfall for the same period last year was 444.7 millimeters, equivalent to 17.51 inches. This year's rainfall is more than one-third higher than last year's.

Late Maturation of Cotton

Excessive rainfall after autumn, coupled with drought before summer, has caused considerable damage to cotton. At first, it could not grow, and then it only grew stems and leaves and did not produce flowers and buds. In the suburbs of Shanghai, Taicang, Kunshan, Baoshan, Qingpu, Songjiang, Fengxian, Nanhui, and other counties, new cotton should have been seen by the middle of the seventh lunar month. However, due to excessive rainfall, it has not yet been seen. There is a saying that "early-growing cotton and late-growing rice," but now that the growth of cotton is like this, the harvest will probably be reduced. However, the early and late rice itself will not be affected.

Ministry of Finance Forbids British-American Tobacco Company from Growing Tobacco in Xuchang; Because It Violates International Conventions; The Company Has Been Warned to Stop Growing

The Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance, in order to improve domestic flue-cured tobacco, established the Xuchang Tobacco Improvement Committee, specializing in planting and other work, and hired experts to study the soil and guide tobacco planting. The results of the experiments were very good. This year, the yield of flue-cured tobacco in Xudi increased by 15% compared with last year. Unexpectedly, the tobacco-rich area was coveted by foreigners. The British-American Tobacco Company in this city, without the permission of the central government, set up tobacco-growing places in the area without authorization. The Taxation Department found out about this situation and reported it to the Ministry of Finance for verification. It is now learned that the Ministry of Finance believes that the company's weighing of tobacco in the area is a violation of international commercial treaties and has warned the company to stop planting.

First, the preparatory committee reported on the preparatory process, the collection of share capital, and the Shanghai Special City Party Department's approval for the newspaper's registration, as well as transferring letters to the Central Propaganda Department. Then, the company's articles of association were approved. Finally, Xiao Tongzi, Yan Esheng, Cheng Shewo, Guan Ji'an, Tian Danfo, Qian Cangshuo, and Wu Zhongyi were elected as seven directors, and Hu Pu'an and Cheng Cangbo were elected as two supervisors. On the afternoon of the 12th at 4 PM, the first board meeting was held at the newspaper hall. All directors attended, and supervisor Hu Pu'an was present. Xiao Tongzi was publicly elected as chairman. The following resolutions were made: (1) Approval of the rules of procedure for the board of directors and the general organization outline of the newspaper hall; (2) Election of Yan Esheng, Tian Danfo, and Qian Cangyu as standing directors; (3) Election of Yan Esheng as general manager and Tian Danfo as manager. It is said that the newspaper is now actively preparing for publication.

In order to revive the market and pay attention to public health, the citizens of this city requested the Municipal Council to fill all unfilled riverbanks in the city to prevent residents from discarding filth into the riverbanks, which would cause epidemics and harm public health. Fire at the Doutian Small Temple in Pudong

At 46 Jijiadu Ferry, Pudong, there is a two-story building with a Doutian Small Temple inside. Yesterday evening at 6 PM, when the monks were performing rituals elsewhere, the temple was empty. For unknown reasons, a fire suddenly broke out on the upper floor of the back building, and flames quickly burst through the roof. Zhao Longsheng, director of the Pudong Fire Brigade, heard the report and immediately led his team to rush to the scene to extinguish the fire. Thanks to the effective water supply, the flames were quickly extinguished. One room on the upper floor of the temple was destroyed. Afterwards, the Yangjiadu Police Station took the presiding monk, Pu Qing, into custody for questioning.

Celebrities in the City Hold Tea Party to Welcome Mei Lanfang Yesterday: Mayor Wu and the Russian Ambassador Give Speeches: Mr. Mei Elaborates on His Visit to Russia

Yesterday afternoon at 4 PM, celebrities from all walks of life in the city held a tea party at the International Hotel on the second floor to welcome Dr. Mei Lanfang, who returned with honors from his European tour. Many guests attended, including Mayor Wu and Russian Ambassador Hu Die. Dr. Mei also reported on his performance during his European tour. The details are as follows:

Attending Guests

The guests who attended the tea party yesterday included Mayor Wu, the Russian Ambassador, Dr. Mei, Hu Die, Chen Qicai, Yang Hu, Yu Ming, Yu Shangyuan, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Li Denghui, Wang Boqi, Xu Xinliu, Lin Kanghou, Feng Gengguang, Chen Zheqing, Huang Renzhi, Li Dachao, Zhu Shaoping, Luo Mingyou, Pan Guangjiong, and other Chinese and foreign guests, totaling over 200 people. Mayor Wu presided over the event, and Pan Guangjiong translated.

Mayor's Speech

During the event, Chairman Mayor Wu stood up and delivered a speech, stating that "We are holding this tea party today to welcome Dr. Mei back to the country. Dr. Mei was invited to perform in the Soviet Union, which is of great significance. I believe that the harmonious relationship between people requires mutual understanding. Dr. Mei's trip to the Soviet Union not only communicated art but also promoted diplomatic relations, which is of profound significance. Therefore, from the perspective of our country, the gains are very large. On the one hand, it can make the Soviet people have a deeper understanding of our country, and at the same time, it can promote cultural cooperation and closer diplomatic relations between the two sides. This is all due to Mr. Mei's efforts. Dr. Mei has been exposed to European culture, and he must have benefited a lot personally. In the future, Chinese art will rely on Mr. Mei to promote and carry it forward. We have specially set up this meeting to express our gratitude, and we are honored to have the Russian Ambassador and guests participating. I would also like to take this opportunity to thank the Russian authorities for their hospitality and ask the Russian Ambassador to convey our gratitude to your country." After the speech, Pan Guangjiong translated it into English.

Russian Ambassador's Speech

The Russian Ambassador then gave a speech, stating that "I am very honored to participate in this grand banquet today. I met Dr. Mei and Ms. Hu Die in Moscow and appreciated Chinese drama. I introduced Dr. Mei to the art circles of our country, who expressed their admiration for the greatness of Chinese opera. I believe that the goodwill between the two countries should be based on cultural ties. Mr. Mei's trip has been very effective. The advancement of new culture should be based on old knowledge. Therefore, the people of our country express their unlimited welcome to Mr. Mei's trip. We also hope that Mr. Mei will bring Russian culture to exchange with us. At this time of cultural movement, its importance is as serious as political issues and economic issues, and its methods can be divided into (1) integrating and studying the cultures of various countries with our own culture to seek integration and development, (2) maintaining our own culture and carrying out unilateral promotion. I think the former is more appropriate, so Mr. Mei's exchange of your country's culture to us is enough to arouse the interest of our people, promote international understanding, and increase human happiness." After the speech, Pan Guangjiong translated it into Chinese.

Wang's Speech

At the invitation of Chairman Wu, Wang Xiaolai stood up and gave a speech, stating, "The previous welcome and farewell parties were all about bringing things back from foreign investigations and research, creating an import surplus. Mr. Mei's trip is a special case, taking things out, so I feel very honored. Chinese culture originated very early and is inevitably outdated, but past achievements cannot be obliterated. Mr. Mei's welcome in the Soviet Union shows that our country's status is still preserved. After returning, I hope Mr. Mei will help to revitalize the opera to help the disaster victims, and I hope to continue to work hard to improve our Chinese opera."

Mayor's Introduction

Mayor Wu then stood up and introduced Dr. Mei's speech, saying that "Mr. Mei returned to Europe early because he saw that the domestic flood situation was serious and could not be ignored. He specifically planned to perform charity performances to help the disaster. All our citizens should not only support the progress but also try to raise funds. In the Yangtze River Basin, among the 290 counties in Hubei, Jiangxi, Anhui, and other provinces, 150 counties have been affected by the disaster, and the flood is even worse than in the 20th year of the Republic of China. Although Shanghai is temporarily safe, it will inevitably be affected in the future. Everything must be calculated on a large scale and not rejected for small profits. Shanghai is like a fish, and other places are like water. If the water dries up, the fish will die. Only when business develops can the market prosper. I hope that everyone will immediately rescue the disaster victims."

Mei's Speech

Dr. Mei Lanfang then stood up and said, "In February of this year, Lanfang was hired by the Soviet Cultural Association to bring our troupe to perform in Russia. After finishing, I also traveled to Europe with Mr. Yu Shangyuan. When I set off, Mayor Wu and other gentlemen bid farewell to Lanfang here. Now, I am honored by the grand deception of the gentlemen, and Mayor Wu and others have praised Lanfang so much, which makes Lanfang very ashamed and grateful. Recalling that when the Soviet government formally invited Lanfang last year, I was quite suspicious and even panicked, because the Soviet Union is the most developed country in the world in terms of drama. Can Chinese opera be shown to others? Is there any value in studying it? It always felt like a question. Later, because the government and Ambassador Yan and the public of the Shanghai Drama Advancement Association all believed that it was a great intention of the Soviet government and that it had something to do with the culture and diplomacy of the two countries, they were all very enthusiastic. Therefore, Lanfang also gained a lot of courage. Before making a decision, Lanfang also talked to Ambassador Bao several times. Ambassador Bao also believed that Chinese opera has many characteristics and can be introduced to the Soviet Union. Moreover, Ambassador Bao said that the Soviet people wanted to study Chinese drama very much and were very sincere and hoped I would go. So Lanfang thought that I could not live up to their kindness, so I decided to take the risk to go. Lanfang departed from Shanghai on February 21st. The weather along the way was not very cold. I arrived in Moscow on February 12th. After resting in Moscow for a few days, I went on stage to perform. On the opening day, the Soviet government asked Ambassador Yan to give a public speech to the people on stage, and Mr. Arosif, the president of the Cultural Association, introduced me on stage. These are all very memorable. We performed in Russia, and every day the audience was very crowded for eight days. Later, because many people had not heard it yet, the Cultural Association came to me to discuss and repeatedly asked me to sing for a few more days. I agreed at the time, so I continued to perform for seven days, for a total of fifteen days. During the performance, the Soviet people expressed a very enthusiastic attitude towards us. I heard that TASS and the Central News Agency sent many telegrams, and the domestic newspapers published them in detail. I won't say much now. What is more important is that those famous Soviet playwrights and writers published in major newspapers have many comments on Chinese opera. They discovered many advantages in Chinese opera. Now I will simply say a few words about what they said. They said that the biggest advantage of Chinese opera can be roughly divided into three points: First, Chinese opera contains singing, dialogue, dancing, and martial arts. It is a comprehensive art. They all think this is a feature of Chinese opera. The second is that Chinese opera is most in line with the principle of stage economy. For example, to represent a boat in Chinese opera, you only need to use a paddle to represent a boat, and you can make many, many postures on the water. If you really want to get a real boat, I'm afraid it won't be so convenient, and the impression gained in the eyes of the audience is the same boat, but on the stage, the difference between "economy" and "non-economy" is distinguished. So this point is also what they think is very long. The third point is that Chinese actors' training is very profound. One day, we held a research meeting at the Drama Association. We showed them the various stages and various skill trainings that Chinese actors have gone through during the period of learning opera. So they all know that in Chinese opera, every actor has to go through six or seven years of training before they can go on stage. Every move on the stage, such as stage steps and posture, is very strict and has a certain current law. It is called having a place and a size, and it cannot be ambiguous at all, but a kind of vigorous application is all in the actor's talent. These points are all praised by them. Mr. Meyerhold, the most famous playwright in the Soviet Union, said that he will also adopt this method of Chinese opera to compile and perform their plays in the future, and said that it can be realized soon. There is also Mr. Eisenstein, a world-famous film director, who also said that the method of Chinese opera can be used in films. Although they said that, Lanfang is still not confident about how Chinese opera is. If these two people's remarks can be seen in reality, then there may be a little influence on the culture of the two countries. I have briefly reported on the situation of performing opera in Russia. As for their comments on Chinese opera, there are many in the newspapers, and it is impossible to finish them all at once. I plan to translate it in the future and use it as our reference. As for Lanfang, I am very grateful for their kind hospitality in the Soviet Union this time. In advance, their government organized a reception committee to publicize to the people. When we set off, we took a special ship sent by the Soviet Union, and there were party representatives traveling with us to take care of us along the way. After arriving in Vladivostok, the Cultural Association sent representatives to welcome us again. When we arrived in Moscow, the people expressed their welcome, which shows a friendly expression between the governments and people of the two countries. Therefore, Lanfang is grateful to Ambassador Bao, the representative of the Soviet Union, today. After Lanfang performed in Russia, he went to Central Europe to travel. Because the time was very short, it was just a quick glance. I saw about seventy or eighty plays. In short, the dramas of various countries have their own styles and cannot be generalized. As for me, I stayed in Russia for a relatively long time. Russia is originally the most distant country in the world in terms of drama. Since the revolution, their government has used all its energy to create new dramas, but at the same time, for their old drama culture, they still preserve it in the old way. The temperament of the Russian people is very determined, and they are willing to work hard on everything. They are also like this for drama. Just say that there are more than 70 theaters in Moscow alone, and there are more than 200 drama schools in the country, with more than 29,000 students. With such efforts, I think there will definitely be new gains and great success in the future. The spirit of the Russian people's brave advance is really admirable. As for the other construction situation, we don't need to say much. Just looking at this point of drama, we can imagine it. After Lanfang went to Europe this time, looking at other people's operas and thinking about my own operas, I think that if China can go through strict selection and new improvements, it will definitely have a higher status in the future. However, this responsibility is very great, and it is by no means what Lanfang alone or the strength of our drama circles can do. I still hope that all the enthusiastic gentlemen in the society who love drama will come together to sort it out, so that our Chinese drama may have a more developed day. Regarding the experience of going abroad this time and the detailed situation of the European drama circles, Lanfang plans to write it out in the future and ask the gentlemen for advice. Today, I can only say a few words. If there is anything that is not enough, I have to ask the gentlemen to forgive me. Today, I thank you all for your kindness. Lanfang still has one thing to ask of you all. Lanfang heard on the way back to the country that the disaster situation in various provinces was extremely serious, and I was very anxious. When I returned to Shanghai, I heard that Mr. Xu Junren, Mr. Wang Yishi, and Mr. Du Yuesheng told me about the flood situation, which was very tragic. Lanfang volunteered to perform charity performances for a relatively long time to do my best. Mr. Xu, Wang, and Du all agreed and promised that the charity association would quickly organize it. It can be performed on stage after it cools down in autumn. However, Lanfang is weak, the disaster situation is extremely serious, and the market is not good. Therefore, it is necessary to ask all the gentlemen for help. If you can save more money, the disaster victims can get more benefits. Lanfang will be very grateful."

Hu Die's Speech

Finally, the chairman introduced Ms. Hu Die's speech, saying that Chinese drama is different from foreign drama, especially movies. Ms. Hu is engaged in movies, and she must have benefited a lot from her trip to Russia. Ms. Hu then stood up and briefly said, "I have successively reported the detailed experience of this European tour. Now I will briefly describe my feelings as follows: The Soviet Union and European countries all use movies as a tool for education and propaganda, dividing them into categories and projecting them on the screen. The interest is good and the effect is great. I hope that our country will immediately follow suit to seek development. At the same time, I am very grateful for the hospitality and welcome from the authorities, and I would like to take this opportunity to thank Ambassador Bao and ask you to convey my humble opinion to your country. In addition, I also hope that everyone present will give me guidance from time to time to correct my shortcomings."

Following the Welcome to Mei

The tea party ended at 6 PM. It is reported that Russian Ambassador Bogomolov will host a dinner at the Russian Embassy at 8:30 PM today to entertain Dr. Mei and invite celebrities from all walks of life in the city to accompany him. At 5 PM on the 23rd of this month, Mrs. Freitz of the International Drama Society of Shanghai will hold a tea party at Sassoon Villa at 4391 Hongqiao Road to welcome Dr. Mei. In addition, playwright Yu Shangyuan was originally scheduled to return to the north a few days ago, but due to entertainment and private affairs, the trip was delayed. It is said that he will leave Shanghai after the 23rd.

The second Sino-German Express ship "Bosten" of the North German Company, managed by the German Meizuishi Foreign Firm, is coming to Shanghai from Germany for the first time. It has already sailed from Hong Kong yesterday and will arrive in Shanghai tomorrow. It will be open to public viewing from the 17th. I will repeat the following:

Late Arrival

The second new ship "Bosten" of the North German Company set sail from Hengbao on July 5th and was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the 6th of this month. Later, because the ship's parts were damaged en route, the repair was delayed, delaying the trip by ten days. It was not until yesterday that the ship sent a telegram to Shanghai, stating that it would leave Hong Kong on the 14th and is expected to arrive in Shanghai at noon on the 16th. Because the ship was late, the sailing schedule to Japan was changed to the 19th, and the sailing schedule to Europe from Shanghai was changed to September 1st for export.

Import

Yesterday, the Meizuishi Foreign Firm had already prepared a pilot to lead the "Bosten" into port when it arrived outside the Tongsha beach at the mouth of Wusong. This time, it still needs to be open to the public for viewing, so the ship is still moored at the Gonghexing Wharf in Hongkou as usual. Yesterday, the firm had already sent out invitations, and the viewing period is on the 17th and 18th. There are a total of fifty passengers coming to Shanghai on this ship, and others to various ports are also full. There are many goods.

Crowded with Passengers

The "Bosten" is a thousand tons smaller than the "Xiangshiswan" ship. The format layout and equipment of the ship are the same as those of the "Xianghuosituo" ship. It is also powered by electricity. It is the most modern in the Far East. There are a total of two hundred and ninety-four first and second class rooms. It only takes twenty-three days to go to Europe from Shanghai, so the tickets were sold out a month ago. This time, Cheng Tianfang, the newly appointed Chinese minister to Germany, and his entourage of more than ten people went to the firm to buy tickets to take office in Germany. Yesterday Morning - High Tide Exceeded Forecast - 12 Feet 1 Inch, Half a Foot Higher than Predicted - Yangtze River Water Level Gradually Decreasing, Night Navigation Resumed

The high tide that occurred in this city at 0:05 AM yesterday was higher than the predicted 11 feet 5 inches 6 points. According to the Shuipu (River Dredging) Bureau's water level marker, it reached 12 feet 1 inch, one minute earlier than the predicted time of 0:06 AM. This means it was 5 inches 4 points higher than predicted. Therefore, when the tide was rising rapidly, the water flow in the Huangpu River was turbulent and quite dangerous. Some ditches on the lower roads had water gushing out of the pipes due to the water flow.

Warehouses Unaffected - However, the height of the embankment along the north side of the Jianghai Customs Wharf is above 13 feet, so there was still a difference of nine inches (eight inches six points). Recently, various companies and banks have already intensified their protection of warehouses, so there was no impact.

Night Navigation Resumed - Furthermore, the Jianghai Customs forwarded Jianghan Customs River Patrol Commissioner's Yangtze River Downstream Shipping Notice No. 2510: "Previously, due to the Yangtze River flooding, both banks were submerged. For the sake of navigation safety, this office issued Yangtze River Downstream Shipping Notice No. 2494, prohibiting ships from navigating at night. Now, it has been found that the water level is gradually decreasing, and the ban is no longer necessary. The ban will be lifted when the Wuhan (Hankou) water level drops to 13.106 meters (43.0 English feet). This notice has been submitted to the Customs Commissioners of various ports downstream for approval and record. Therefore, this notice is issued to all shipping merchants for their information. Commissioner Bai Lieshi."

Carpenter Sues Doctor - For Unilaterally Amputating a Hand - But the Hospital Has a Signature from the Carpenter - Trial Opened Yesterday, Court Still Needs to Investigate

Lu Mingyao, a 28-year-old native of Jiangdu and graduate of Tongde Medical School, recently opened Tongji Hospital at the intersection of Chengdu Road and Dagu Road, but did not obtain a license from the Municipal Health Bureau to practice medicine. He is now being sued by Shen Yuji, a carpenter from Taixing residing at No. 41, Diandang Lane, Dadongmen, Nanshi, through lawyer Zhang Deyou, for negligent injury. A civil suit is also attached, seeking compensation of 11,140 yuan. Shen developed a blood tumor on his right wrist in March of this year.

Which Greatly Hindered His Work

Introduced by a friend, Ding Wenqing, he went to Lu's clinic for treatment on July 11. They agreed on a consultation fee of 30 yuan. Lu then used a knife to cut off the tumor, accidentally damaging a blood vessel, causing uncontrollable bleeding. Seeing that there was no way to save it, Lu sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment without Shen's consent, and Lu unilaterally had Shen's right hand amputated. At the time, Shen was in a coma due to excessive blood loss. When he woke up, he discovered that his hand had been amputated. But Shen's family relied entirely on Shen's work for sustenance. Now that his

Hand Has Been Amputated

He cannot work. Therefore, he is suing him under Article 284 of the Criminal Law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Risheng of the First Special Court opened the Criminal Division II for questioning. According to Shen Yuji, he explained the previous situation, and said, "At that time, Lu claimed that after treatment, I would be able to work as usual in a little over a month. Who knew that after the operation, the bleeding would not stop, and the pain was extreme, and I fell into a coma. Lu then said that the hospital's equipment was incomplete, and sent me to Renji Hospital by car, without my consent, and had my hand amputated.

That Is Why I Am Suing"

etc. In response, Lu Mingyao stated that the plaintiff was introduced by Ding Wenqing and came to the clinic for treatment. At that time, I said that this hand could not be cured unless it was amputated. However, the plaintiff repeatedly begged me to try to save the hand and find a way to treat it. I then cut off the tumor and saw that the bone had turned black and was completely rotten. If it was not amputated, it would endanger his life. After I persuaded him, the plaintiff also agreed, so I sent him to Renji Hospital by car, where Dr. Lai performed the surgery to amputate it. At that time, the plaintiff

Signed in Person

And hired lawyer Wang Shouan to defend him and filed a counterclaim, accusing Shen of obstructing his reputation, threatening, etc. Judge Huang then stated that the court had already investigated with Renji Hospital, and the hospital replied that the plaintiff and a guarantor, Zhang Guoxiang, had both signed before the hand was amputated. He then asked Shen Yuji about this, but Shen completely denied it, saying that he was already in a coma at the time, how could he have signed? The court considered that the case still needed to be investigated and adjourned the hearing.

Japanese Fraudster - Commits Suicide in Hangzhou West Lake

According to the Daily News yesterday, on July 11 of this year, Asatani Toshio and Fujii Yoneichi arrived in Shanghai from Nagasaki and stayed at the Hiroshima Hotel on Wusong Road. Asatani falsely claimed to be proficient in automobile manufacturing and to have been running a car dealership in the South Seas for many years. He also claimed to have eight cars in Shanghai and defrauded various parties. Fujii, who was with him, borrowed 150 yuan from him. On July 22, he suddenly disappeared. Unexpectedly, he had gone to Hangzhou and stayed at the Wenhu Hotel in Geling, West Lake, living lavishly. He also used fraudulent means, falsely claiming to be running a car business in Shanghai and using the alias Chen Songji from Taiwan. Eventually, his evil deeds caught up with him, and he committed suicide by taking poison. The Japanese Consulate General in this city has received the investigation details from the Consulate in Hangzhou. The owner of the Hiroshima Hotel also received a suicide note from the perpetrator. According to Mr. Yamashita Tokuichi, the owner of the hotel, Asatani was from Hyogo Prefecture and was fluent in Chinese.

Child Addicted to Opium - Abandoned by the Roadside, Gasping for Breath, on the Verge of Death - Revived Only After Drinking Medicated Water

Zhou Caifu of Ningbo, at around 8:00 AM on the 11th of this month, was walking past the entrance of Lane 180, Rue Wagner in the French Concession, when he noticed a male child, about two years old, lying on the ground, gasping for breath, on the verge of death, seemingly abandoned. He immediately reported it to the Qianshan Road Police Station, and Detective Chen Yulin was dispatched to investigate. The child was sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment and reported back to the police chief. After examination by a doctor, it was determined that the child was not ill, but was addicted to opium. Due to the withdrawal symptoms, he was mentally exhausted. After giving him opium substitute medicine, the child gradually woke up and returned to normal, crying and laughing as usual. However, he could not speak clearly and could not tell his name, address, or the reason why he was abandoned. The hospital notified the police station, and after investigation by Detective Chen in various places, it was learned that the child was the son of Yang Heshang, who was engaged in the manufacture of red pills. Last November, he was arrested by the Public Concession Police for manufacturing red pills and sent to the First Special District Court, where he was sentenced to one year in prison. Yang's wife was addicted to opium and red pills, which was passed on to the child. She had to give the child opium every day to satisfy his addiction, otherwise he would cry and make noise incessantly. Recently, Yang's wife suddenly disappeared, and there was no one to take care of the child. It is unknown how he was abandoned on the roadside. At around 10:00 AM yesterday, the police station ordered Detective Chen to take the child to the Criminal Division VIII of the Second Special District Court for instructions. Lawyer Yao of the Police Affairs Department explained the previous situation. After Judge Sun Pengxian questioned Detective Chen Yulin about the investigation, he ordered the bailiff to take the child to the orphanage to be raised. However, when the child was brought to the court, the detective feared that he would experience withdrawal symptoms and be mentally exhausted, so he prepared a small cup of opium water for him to drink. Otherwise, if the child was not given opium water after two hours, his mind would immediately fall into a state of coma. This is indeed an interesting event in the addiction scene.

Robbery of Pawnshop - Gunshot Murder of Shop Assistant - Conclusion of Interrogation - Awaiting Scheduled Verdict

Wang Xiangxun, a Chaozhou native and shop assistant at the Jixing Pawnshop at No. 640, Haining Road, was shot in the head and killed by robbers at 9:55 PM on the 28th of last month. After investigation by Chinese Detectives Jin Haibo, Wang Guangqi, and Hu Guangrong of the Hongkou Police Station, Wu Zhenrong from Zhenjiang, Chen Zhengmao from Shaoxing, and Wu Agou from Suzhou were arrested and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. The details have been reported in this newspaper many times. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Criminal Division III. Lawyer Wang Yaotang of the Bureau of Public Works stated that before the incident, the group gathered in Room 28 of the Huzhou Hotel at No. 4, Lane 19, North Shanxi Road. At that time, Wu Zhenrong was carrying a handgun and went to Haining Road, first intending to rob the Dada Pawnshop. Seeing that there was no screen to block the view, he feared that pedestrians on the road would notice, so he changed his plan and robbed the Jixing Pawnshop, resulting in this tragedy. The handgun was made in France, with the number 205, and had a total of five bullets. After the incident, it was hidden at the residence of Wu's sister at No. 1, Lujia Ferry, Pudong, and has been recovered. There were four bullets inside, one of which was the bullet that entered Wang Xiangxun's brain, etc. He then presented the handgun for inspection and requested investigation. Wu Zhenrong confessed that he bought the handgun from a friend surnamed Yang for 40 yuan. He initially asked the deceased for help, but the deceased shouted loudly, so he had to shoot him. Chen Zhengmao confessed that he had previously been imprisoned for seven years for robbery. He met Wu Zhenrong in prison, who invited him to rob together, and he acted as a lookout outside. Wu Agou confessed that he stayed at the Tongshang and Huzhou hotels with Wu Zhenrong before the incident. At that time, they were penniless, had no money for dinner, and were hungry. They went together under the pretext of pawning clothes, grabbed the deceased's hand, forced him to hand over silver dollars, but failed. Wu then fired the gun, and he took the opportunity to escape, which was the truth. Judge Xiao Fen concluded that they should be returned to custody and scheduled a verdict.

French Concession - Busts Illegal Smelting of Inferior Silver Coins - Manufacturing Silver Ingots for Sale - More Than 20 Male and Female Criminals Arrested

In recent days, the French Police have received numerous confidential reports stating that a large number of lawless elements in the concession have established a large-scale illegal smelting organization to smelt inferior silver coins and mix them into the market, harming countless people. The method they use is to first send out accomplices to buy inferior silver coins at low prices from small money shops and cigarette paper exchange shops. After smelting them, they are made into various silver ingots and sold privately in large quantities or transported to other ports, which affects the financial situation of this city. After receiving the report, the police authorities immediately ordered their subordinates to conduct a thorough investigation. It was not until around 2:00 AM yesterday that they discovered that the main organizational center was secretly located in the house at No. 117, Rue de la Paille. The police chief immediately dispatched a large number of detectives in disguise to surround and arrest them. They seized tens of thousands of yuan worth of inferior silver on the spot and arrested more than 20 male and female key criminals. However, the main culprit has not yet been arrested, and the police are continuing to search for him.

China-France Pharmacy Donates Profits to Disaster Relief

The Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Disaster Relief in Various Provinces received a letter from the China-France Pharmacy on August 9, which stated: "Dear Sirs, Since the beginning of summer this year, there has been continuous rain, mountain torrents, and outbreaks of disasters in the Yangtze, Huai, and Yellow Rivers. The severity of the damage is even worse than the flood of 20 years ago, and relief is urgently needed. Although our pharmacy is weak and has limited capabilities, we dare not lag behind others in our desire to do good. We have decided to hold a one-month profit-sharing disaster relief campaign starting on the 10th of this month to promote this cause. Although we know that a cup of water cannot save a cartload of burning fuel, there are many shops in Shanghai, and if they can gradually implement this, the amount will be considerable and will be of some help. In addition to reporting the total amount raised after one month, we are sending this letter in advance for your information." From this, we can see the pharmacy's enthusiasm for relief efforts.

Banking Association - Publication of the Banking Practice Series - Compiled by Zhou Yangwen

In order to impart practical banking knowledge to those aspiring to study banking, the Banking Association has commissioned senior bank employees with knowledge and experience to write various banking books, named the Banking Practice Series. "Domestic Remittance and Negotiation Business" (內匯兌及押匯業務), one of the books in the series, was published by the Commercial Press a few days ago. This book was written by Mr. Zhou Yangwen, who has 20 years of banking experience and is currently the Assistant Manager and Director of the Real Estate Department of the New China Trust and Savings Bank. It consists of 10 series, 240 pages thick, and a total of 200,000 words. It covers all the procedures, forms, and documents for domestic remittance and negotiation business, and is particularly detailed in the transfer of funds between branches. The Shanghai Reserve of the Four Banks issued a preparation report stating that the Four Banks Reserve is jointly established by the Yanye (Salt Industry), Jin Cheng, Zhongnan, and Continental Banks to exclusively handle the issuance of banknotes from the Zhongnan Bank. According to the reserve's issuance regulations, banknotes are issued with full reserve, with a cash reserve of at least 60% and a guarantee reserve of up to 40%. It is announced once a week, inspected by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. The 293rd announcement of the Shanghai Reserve on August 10, 1935, is recorded as follows: Amount of banknotes in circulation: 19,200,273 yuan. Total reserve amount: 19,200,273 yuan, including cash reserve of 17,058,693 yuan and guarantee reserve of 2,144,080 yuan.

The 67th inspection was held at the bank on August 10, 1935, and the inspection results are listed as follows: Total amount of exchange coupons issued: 3,095,310 yuan and 5 jiao, including silver dollar coupons: 2,640,385 yuan and 7 jiao, subsidiary coin coupons: 454,924 yuan and 8 jiao. Total exchange coupon reserve fund: 3,095,310 yuan and 5 jiao, including cash reserve of silver dollars: 2,151,150 yuan and 5 jiao, guarantee reserve converted into silver dollars: 944,160 yuan. According to Article 2 of the Zhejiang Local Bank Exchange Coupon Regulations, the issuance of exchange coupons requires 60% cash reserve and 40% guarantee reserve. The inspection results show that the cash reserve is above 60% and the guarantee reserve is below 40%, which is consistent with the regulations. This report is hereby made. August 10, 1935. Notes on Trade Association Announcements

Since the New Pharmaceutical Industry Association dispatched Zhou Bangjun, Xu Xiaochu, Yuan Hesong, Zhou Mengbai, Tu Kunhua, Sun Choucheng, and others to Beijing twice to negotiate the revised registration method for patent medicines, Director Liu of the Ministry of Health verbally agreed and instructed them to prepare an official document for formalization. It is now known that the official document has been sent out, with the following general content: "Submitting a request for a revised registration method for patent medicines in order to comply with regulations. Upon investigation, the subordinate association has previously sent representatives to personally explain the business difficulties and request that the registration method for patent medicines be revised. We were honored to have received your approval and instructions to prepare an official request, reflecting your concern for business difficulties. We are extremely grateful. The points that we propose to be revised are listed as follows: (1) Upon investigation, the pharmacies have produced many kinds of patent medicines over the years, ranging from hundreds to dozens. If they are all required to be registered at once, it will be difficult in terms of time and economy. It is requested that special flexibility be given, extending the deadline and appropriately reducing fees. (2) During the registration period, it is feared that the provinces and cities will not understand the central government's intentions. If the patent medicines sold in the market, which are not produced locally but are being sold on behalf, are also required to be registered, there will be many obstacles. It is requested that when notifying the provincial and municipal governments, it be clearly stated that registration is limited to the place of production only, in order to avoid misunderstandings. (3) (Omitted) (4) Registering hundreds of patent medicines at the same time requires a large amount of advance payment of fees. It is requested that only the certificate fee and stamp tax be paid first. All inspection fees, after deducting the originally determined amount, will be paid upon receiving the license, which would make the burden lighter and easier to comply with."

The Glass Industry Association held its 24th joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members yesterday. Wang Rongkun was elected as chairman, and Wu Zhen was the recorder. The important cases resolved are listed below: (1) Committee member Wang Songyuan and others suggested that due to the recent sharp drop in the Shanghai exchange rate, the four-number Chinese-made glass sheets sold at six yuan per box at the settlement market price are resulting in losses. How should the price be raised to maintain profitability? Please decide on a resolution. Resolution: Li Songfang, Zhuang Jusheng, Chai Wenjing, and Lu Gengchen were appointed as four committee members to calculate. They responded that the price should be calculated according to the current market exchange rate. It is proposed to increase the price of four-number Chinese-made glass sheets by 6 yuan, 1 jiao, and 5 fen per box. Notice to all members to comply. (Remaining cases omitted).
