Free Talk

Wrong Characters and Correct Characters

— Tang Tao

Mr. Zhang Taiyan advocated writing correct characters. He believed that people who write vernacular Chinese should have a thorough understanding of "primary school," so that they would not write characters incorrectly. His aim was not small, because he wanted to use this to overthrow vernacular Chinese and bring back classical Chinese. The fatal killer is "primary school."

Being able to have a thorough understanding of "primary school" and carefully study dictionaries and exegesis, just like an antique dealer who is good at identifying old goods and knows their origins, is indeed very good. However, antiques are still antiques. They are only for appreciation, just for display. Perhaps they are still useful to people who want to study ancient social situations, but they have nothing to do with current life. Therefore, the Zhou Ding is still the Zhou Ding, but the things used to pass on the country, decoct medicine, brew tea, and burn incense have all changed their names and appearances. The reason is to meet the needs of life: convenience, precision.

The same is true of writing. The Greater Seal Script of the Zhou Dynasty was very civilized and convenient at that time, but now, elegant people ask Mr. Taiyan to write couplets and hang them in their studies for decoration only. What we use in our daily lives is regular script that has undergone several changes, and there are simplified characters and wrong characters that are changing day by day.

The needs of life determine these things, and no one can do anything about it.

According to the opinions of the gentlemen in the Zhangshi Weekly Lectures, what Mr. Taiyan advocated is the correct character, that is, the "contemporary character" mentioned in the Kangxi Dictionary, not the ancient character. However, there are many characters in the Kangxi Dictionary that we do not use now. What "time" is "contemporary"?

If it is not now, then it only counts as the past.

Mr. Taiyan said in his article "The Relationship Between Vernacular and Classical Chinese":

"Common auxiliary words, such as yan zai hu ye, are not used in vernacular Chinese now, but hu and ye are still used. For example, when you meet an acquaintance and greet them, you say 'hao ya,' ya is the same as hu; when you respond to someone's compliment, you say 'shi ai,' ai is the same as ye. The word fu is used at the end of a sentence in classical Chinese, such as 'bi zi zhi yan fu,' which is the same as ba in vernacular Chinese, with a slight change in pronunciation. Yi changes to li, and the character of Lvsheng in Shuowen, or from the sound of li, can prove this example. The four characters hu ye fu yi have only changed slightly in sound, and logically we should use hu ye fu yi, not ya ai ba li."

It turns out that the "ya ai ba li" that we usually consider to be correct characters are, according to Mr. Taiyan's discovery, actually fabricated wrong characters. Isn't this enough to make those of us who oppose wrong characters feel lost? However, are we going to correct these wrong characters and follow Mr. Taiyan to "hu ye fu yi," or are we going to continue to accommodate spoken language and let it "ya ai ba li" go wrong?

If victory belongs to the latter, then the problem of correct characters and wrong characters is not difficult to solve. Because writing represents or supplements the shortcomings of language, then we should of course require it to accommodate spoken language and make the sound and mouth completely similar. As long as the "sound and mouth" can be "completely similar," it doesn't matter what correct or wrong characters are.

Traveling Through the Gorges (Middle)

— Fang Wu

Along the road, the azure river continuously crashes against the cliffs, creating snowy white splashes, making one's heart feel extraordinarily relaxed and refreshed. Flocks of brown water birds on the river, seeing people coming, fly up to the cliffs in waves, disappearing into the lush green foliage. Sometimes they suddenly swoop down again, skimming lively across the water, emitting joyful calls. How could a traveler feel depressed here, even if unpleasant anxieties were occupying their mind?

At a bend in a hillside, beneath a few ash trees, right next to the river, lies a large rock. Sitting on it is a man in a short black cloth jacket, dangling his feet in the river, leisurely washing them—or rather, playing with them. His expression seems strangely carefree. As soon as my companion saw him, he stopped whistling, raised his hand, as if reporting in, and shouted loudly.

"Hey!"

After another shout, the man slowly turned his face, squinted his right eye, widened his left, carefully looked at us, and responded:

"Oh."

Immediately, he lowered his head, straightened one leg out of the water, and lazily rubbed it with his hand, as if deliberately pretending to be unconcerned.

"Is it... just one?"

"Just one."

"Will it rain?"

"No way!"

"Is there wind coming from that side?"

"No!"

While my companion was exchanging coded language with the man, he casually threw the bundle on his back by the roadside and nodded to me, saying:

"Rest for a while!"

The tone was somewhat like a command, not as polite as it had been in the morning. I had no choice but to mechanically sit down. Seeing a clod of earth exposed in his loosened bundle, I immediately understood into whose hands I had fallen. Because I understood that petty thieves, in order to avoid suspicion on the road, always use some worthless items to make their bundles look large.

When the man took his other foot out of the water, he reached into his pocket for a rolled cigarette, put one in his mouth, offered another to my companion, and another to me, while squinting his eyes, showing a mocking tone as he smiled:

"Have one, you've worked hard to get here, you've really suffered!... "

"It's nothing really? It's the stomach driving me along!"

I tried my best to appear calm, but I couldn't help but feel my heart racing.

"Easy now, your boss is after the big money!"

The man burst out laughing.

Seeing my companion reaching out to pull the bundle beside me, he shook the hand holding the cigarette at him and said:

"Slow down!"

A cruel, yet somewhat self-amused expression appeared on his face. A scar on his neck showed a red hue. Then, smiling, he calmly said to me:

"Friend, do you understand? We're not unreasonable—I must tell you... In this place, whatever anyone has the ability to take is theirs... That bundle (pointing with the hand holding the cigarette at the bundle containing the clod of earth), the cigarette in my pocket... (then taking a puff of the cigarette self-satisfactorily) and there is still some treasure over there (pointing to the leather clump under the weeping willow by the slope)...all depend on your skills…"

Following that, he narrowed his eyes, tilted his head back, and smiled mischievously. The cigarette was stuck on the corner of his mouth, just like an anti-aircraft gun, aiming straight at the sky. Before I could say anything, my companion had already put his words into action, snatching my bundle and opening it. Of course, they had the ability to take my things here and claim them as their own.

Seeing nothing of value inside the bundle, my companion crooked his mouth with the cigarette pipe in it and, without a word, picked up the curled books and ragged clothes, held them two or three feet off the ground, and then suddenly threw them all down, stretching out his dry nose with an air of careful inspection.

The man, who had appeared quite imposing, suddenly became uncomfortable and immediately took the cigarette from his mouth, glared at me, and waved his hand, but still tried to maintain a non-angry expression.

"Friend, let us search you!"

As I pulled my unbuttoned shirt back to cover my chest, the man turned his glaring eyes to my companion (who by this time looked panicky), stared for a while, then flicked off some ash with his finger, curled the corner of his mouth, and scolded regretfully:

"Don't you have eyes, you bumpkin!... Go back to playing with your mud."

My companion, his face flushed red, looked at me angrily and muttered in defense.

"Ugh... Damn it, he even said himself he was going to buy goods, I..."

The man suddenly rolled his eyes and, before he could finish speaking, nimbly jumped behind me, shouting:

"Oh, the cunning fellow, you must have hidden it in the leather."

At the same time, he pushed me aside and immediately explored the place where I had just been sitting with his feet.

I retreated in alarm, stammering to defend myself, while also showing a bit of the primal anger that emerges when one is in danger.

"What do I have? Nothing at all, if you're reasonable, you should go to those with money…"

Seeing that I really had nothing and hearing me say this, the man suppressed the anger that had just erupted, only to retort:

"Okay, then why did you lie to him that you were buying goods? Tell me, why?"

Childhood Companions

— Shen Shengshi

After three years of separation from a companion, one must "look at them with new eyes." How much more so with childhood companions, after a separation of more than ten years? In the process of these ten-odd years (people's affairs cannot withstand such a long period of change), many of those who sat on the same bench in elementary school, who were classmates in the same classroom for three or four years, or who played together at the same school for one or two years, have now all changed in my memory, and changed in a way that surprises me so much that I can't even believe they were my former classmates.

Some old companions also make me think of the feelings evoked by Mr. Feng Zikai's cartoon "Elementary School Classmates."

Once, I saw on the street a classmate who used to attend general courses in the same classroom. Now he was carrying a night soil bucket, holding a dung broom in one hand, swaying his body as he carried a load across the street. Some others opened tofu shops, noodle shops, and wonton shops in the local area. Affected by society, they have long abandoned the state of mind they had when they were studying. Life relentlessly weighs them down, and they struggle painfully. I have always sympathized with them. The various bad customs and habits of society harm those companions who are struggling in life.

I personally saw a female classmate, who was only sixteen years old, and used to attend the same school as me, marry a local gangster and give birth to a large group of children. I dare not think about the pain in her life. I heard when I returned to my hometown the year before last that this woman had already died.

In addition, some old companions now all have solid university diplomas. New Western suits flutter on the streets of their hometown. Knowing full well that I remember fighting with them in elementary school, and playing together morning and night, they now dare not "acknowledge" that I am their classmate. It is obvious that sitting on the same bench, we can't have a very engaging conversation.

They no longer have the same perspective as before, and they have long since replaced their former innocent and amiable hearts. Who would be willing to look back at a poor friend who sells his mouth and his writing?

Those past companions already live in several different worlds from me. There are also some who have become worldly-wise, with a hypocritical face. They understand the various philosophies of dealing with the world: perfunctoriness, taking advantage of convenient situations, singing high-sounding tunes, speculating, and learning a glib tongue. Whenever I see them, I always hate them for exchanging pleasantries about the weather and saying a set of utterly painless, hypocritical words. I can only remain silent and willingly show weakness. I have never been able to learn that "philosophy of dealing with the world" well.

Whenever I think of those past companions in my hometown, I always feel particularly sad and lonely. They (she) all live in different worlds from me. Each person walks on a very different road. Each person's thoughts and opinions will not converge. Everyone looks at the world with different eyes. Perhaps we will never walk together again.

Bless those past companions of mine!

Tragedy by the Sea (Part Four)

— Original by French Author Balzac, Translated by Wang Jiansheng

"Her hair is like that of a fairy. If you ask her, 'Tell me, Pirout' (that is what we call Pirouette, she got her name from Saint Pirouette. Chabrame's first name is Pierre, he is her godfather)—tell me, Pirout', he continued, 'what does Uncle say to you?' She will answer me like this: 'He said nothing to me. —Never—nothing,' 'Well, what did he do?' Always on Sundays he kisses me on the forehead.' 'Then you are not afraid?' 'Why should I be afraid,' she says, 'he is my godfather.' He does not want anyone but me to bring him food."

"Pirout says that when she comes, he also smiles a little, but you might as well say it's like a flash of sunlight in the sea mist, because people say he is as gloomy as a storm."

"But," I said, "you have aroused our curiosity without satisfying it. Do you know what brought him to this state? Is it deep sorrow or repentance? Or madness? Or sin? Is it..."

"Ah, sir, no one understands the bottom line of this matter except my father and me. My mother, who is now dead, was a maid in the home of a judge. Chabrame told the judge the whole story. The people of the port say that the monks who confessed him only gave him certificates of redemption for their confessions. My poor mother, because the judge's parlor was next to the kitchen, overheard Chabrame's conversation unintentionally. She heard about this in the past, and now she is dead, and the judge also heard about this, and now he is also dead. My mother repeatedly told us—my father and me—never to reveal this matter to the residents here, but I can tell you this, I was really horrified that night my mother told us."

"Then tell us this story, my friend! We will never mention it to anyone."

The fisherman looked at us and continued to tell us: "Pierre Chabrame, the one you saw there, is the eldest of the Chabrame family. They have been sailors for generations. From their names, you can know that the sea is often under their control. The one you saw is a fisherman. He has his own skills. He has many small boats. He often rows to catch sardines. He even catches deep-sea fish for fishmongers. If he didn't love his wife so much, he would have built a boat to catch sharks. His wife used to be a beautiful woman, from the Brang region of Courondée—she used to be very glorious—and very kind-hearted. She loved her husband very much, so she never allowed him to leave for a longer period than catching sardines. They lived over there—over there," the fisherman said, after indicating a small island wedged between the dunes and the Courondée marshes away from the seaside, he went up a small hill. "Do you see that house? That's his house. Jacques-Quitte Brang and Chabrame only have one child, a boy. They love him very much—to what extent? —Madam! In short, like an only child. They loved him madly. If their little Jacques-Quitte randomly put something in their soup, forgive me, sirs, they would definitely say it made it taste better. We saw them buying the finest toys for their child in the market. I don't know how many times! Everyone told them it was a stupid thing. Little Chabrame soon realized he could do whatever he wanted, so when he grew up, he would do anything evil. If anyone went to his father and said, 'Your son almost put someone's child to death!' he would just laugh and say, 'Ah! He will definitely be a successful sailor in the future. One day he will be able to command the Emperor's warships.' Or another person would say, 'Pierre Chabrame, do you know that your son has blinded little Mésange's girl?' 'Here will be a boy who deals with girls,' Pierre said. This child had not the slightest flaw in his father's mind, so when he was ten years old, this young beast would fight everyone he met; he had twisted chicken necks for the game and cut open pig bellies. I dare say he really wallowed in blood like a cat! 'He will become a glorious soldier,' Chabrame said. 'He already has a bit of a homicidal habit.'"

Loneliness

— Luo Hong

When silent, a cry of loneliness attacks the heart, tightly gripping it. I look at anything in front of me and laugh alone like a child, but the laughter is so light that I can't even hear it myself. Naturally, I don't lack opportunities to interact with people and be in the midst of excitement, but when I am alone in silence, those contrived appearances, deceptive words, and false smiles flash before my eyes one by one. I try hard to avoid them, but I can't. They stubbornly float before my eyes, and in this way, the feeling of loneliness attacks me. Indeed, I understand that this is a very ordinary thing and that there is no need to revisit it so childishly. Many people have obtained warmth and sustenance through deception and contrivance, and many people have obtained comfort through deception and contrivance. People live by hiding a corner of their soul. Therefore, there is no one who is not lonely.

Every time I suffer alone like a child, secretly blaming others for not deceiving me so much and being so hypocritical towards me, I can't help but smile slightly to myself. This is obviously a smile to comfort myself, but before that smile has subsided, I still feel lonely, and my heart is suffering. I hear people say many comforting words and encouraging words to me, and give me many kind smiles. When those smiles are still lingering in my ears, each person's soul is already so far away, and their actions are also so far away.

People live on so lonely.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Bi-Monthly Health Journal

Neurasthenia

— Dr. Feng Shanliang

The causes of this disease are generally due to excessive physical labor, excessive mental work, smoking, alcoholism, seminal emission, masturbation, gonorrhea, and excessive indulgence in sexual desire, etc.

This disease is divided into cerebral neurasthenia and spinal neurasthenia. In cerebral neurasthenia, the symptoms are often headache, heaviness of the head, blurred vision, tinnitus, insomnia, forgetfulness, dramatic emotional changes, loss of appetite, and inability to engage in mental work. In spinal neurasthenia, the common symptoms are feeling tired upon waking up in the morning, muscles in the lower body easily feeling fatigued when walking, unusual sensations in the lower limbs from time to time, and the most obvious symptom is frequent pain in the sacral region. In addition, there are those with premature ejaculation and impotence, which are all signs of sexual neurasthenia.

To treat this disease, in addition to the patient needing to eliminate the inducing causes of the disease, the health of the living environment is also very important, such as—choosing the most convenient and practical methods, such as moderating work and rest, exercising properly, establishing regular eating times, avoiding irregular living, having proper thoughts, ceasing sexual desires, being cautious in socializing, and choosing appropriate nutritional products to ensure that the body and mind achieve tranquility and freedom. Everyone knows that phosphorus is one of the main drugs for treating this disease because phosphorus is an essential medicine for tonifying the nerves. If the human body consumes too much phosphorus, it must seek adequate supplementation. There are many phosphorus preparations for replenishing the nervous system sold on the market, but the only one I appreciate in clinical practice is An Er Shen because that medicine contains particularly strong phosphorus and does not have any drawbacks, making it easy for weakened nerves to return to normal. The lecithin that is so popular nowadays, namely egg yolk phospholipid, is known to be used for quitting smoking, but it is not known that it is actually much more effective for this disease than for quitting smoking. If significant sexual neurasthenia is present, then endocrine hormone preparations are an indispensable supplement. In addition to drug treatment, electromedical therapy also has considerable value, but when seeking medical treatment, the patient's own treatment is also indispensable, and it is necessary to discard worldly affairs to allow the body and mind to achieve absolute freedom. Then, no matter how serious the condition, it is not difficult to return to normal. Nervous Stomach Pain

— Dr. She Lei

Excessive stomach acid, chronic persistent gastric juice leakage, and periodic persistent gastric juice leakage can all cause abnormal gastric secretion nerves, thereby causing stomach pain. However, there are many causes of nervous stomach pain, not just the above-mentioned ones. For example, abnormalities in the gastric motor nerves and sensory nerves can also cause this disease. This article only discusses excessive stomach acid. Excessive stomach acid means that the acidity of the stomach contents is greater than normal. Sometimes organic changes in stomach diseases can also cause this disease, which will not be discussed in detail here. The causes of this disease are generally due to chronic intestinal diseases, bile secretion disorders, reproductive organ disorders, excessive smoking and drinking, and prolonged consumption of irritants. In addition, mental fatigue and depression are also inducing factors for this disease. Patients often feel discomfort in the stomach, pressure, and stomach pain. Stomach pain usually occurs two to three hours after eating. In addition, there are acid reflux, heartburn, and acidic belching. The characteristic of this disease is that it is immediately relieved by taking alkaline agents. The most important thing in the dietary therapy of this disease is fat. Fat can reduce acidity and is also the most effective nutritional product for weak patients. Among fatty foods, milk is the best. Other foods that can irritate the gastric mucosa and enhance gastric acid secretion are all prohibited. In terms of mechanical therapy, gastric lavage is quite effective. Acute Gonorrhea

— Dr. Cui Fuqing

After an incubation period of about two to five days after contracting gonorrhea, the initial symptoms are discovered. Sometimes they may be slightly earlier or later. Once the initial symptoms appear, the sensation in the urethral opening, the navicular fossa, and the area tightly connected to the glans is slightly abnormal. There is occasional mild itching. The glans feels warm, and there is a sensation like ants crawling. The penis feels heavy and tense. The navicular fossa and perineum may have stabbing pains. The spermatic cord and testicles may be pulled and ache dully. Inflammation inside the urethra is not enough to induce sexual excitement, so the penis often erects, and urination is frequent. Each time you urinate, it feels warmer than usual. The pain is worse after urination. After about two to four days, the labia of the urethral opening gradually swell, resulting in a kind of luster. The mucous membrane of the urethral opening turns red, followed by papillae protruding. At this time, if you squeeze the urethral opening up and down with your thumb and forefinger, you will see a small amount of viscous liquid leaking out. If you don't have it after urinating for a while, the viscous liquid will stick to the two lips of the urethral opening and close it. When urinating, the previous sensation of heat is now burning. If you test the urine, you will see things mixed in that look like silk or snow. These are all mixtures of epithelial mucus and pus cells. Then the inflammation becomes more severe. The urethral mucosa swells. Secretion is also becoming more severe. The base of the glans and the navicular fossa all develop tenderness. There is frequent urgency to urinate. Every urination is painful and burning. A large amount of pus is secreted from the urethral opening. When treating this disease, in addition to absolute rest and abstinence from irritating foods, drug therapy is required. Silver preparations are commonly used externally for sterilization. But the one that is recommended now is Lindu Shuyao Er. For internal use, Meisha Lin from Mei Ling Western Firm is recommended. Among the injectable pigments, An De Xue Qing and Tuo Lü Pa Fu Laven are the best. Among the vaccines, mixed serum vaccine is superior. The direct tube shortwave electrotherapy machine and the latest turbid therapy machine are especially effective for acute gonorrhea. Eczema

— Doctor Sun Zhiyao

Eczema is a type of inflammatory skin disease, characterized by itchy skin inflammation. The affected skin area is red and swollen, with small blisters, papules, or pustules appearing on it. This eczema may be scattered or clustered, and the skin surface is often moist and crusty. Eventually, scales fall off, gradually leading to healing. If it persists without treatment, the skin may become infiltrated and thickened, becoming chronic. Auspitz described eczema as a superficial catarrhal disease of the skin. There are two causes of this disease: (1) External causes, such as chemical, thermal, or mechanical irritation; (2) Internal causes, such as adenopathy, chronic gastrointestinal diseases, and nervous system disorders. Menstrual irregularities, diabetes, kidney disease, liver disease, anemia, and weakened individuals are also at risk of developing this condition. From onset to complete cure, the condition can be divided into six stages based on its presentation: 1. Erythematous stage: The skin is red and swollen. 2. Papular stage: Papules appear due to cell infiltration, causing itching. 3. Vesicular stage: In addition to cell infiltration, plasma exudation occurs, accumulating under the stratum corneum to form blisters containing watery, transparent fluid. 4. Pustular stage: The contents become turbid due to the presence of pus cells in the blisters. 5. Moist or Crusty stage: The blister or pustule membranes rupture due to scratching or friction, and the pus drains out, forming a crust. 6. Scaling stage: This is when the eczema is completely healed. For external medication, MISULZINE is the best, as it can penetrate deep into the skin layers and exert a powerful antibacterial effect. This medicine does not stain clothes and has a pleasant scent, making it truly an ideal skin remedy. Available at: Ren Shou Pharmacy, No. 1 Laodehang Lane, Mintini Road, Baixianqiao, French Concession, Shanghai. Price: One yuan per box, plus one yuan for postage. Dr. Wu Sheng, a skin disease specialist, frequently uses this medicine in his practice, demonstrating its value.

Talking Points

Preparing Labor Insurance

— Qiongsheng

Nanjing, 11th (Special Dispatch): The Ministry of Industry is preparing for labor insurance and has drafted a Labor Insurance Law, which has been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and will be sent to the Central Political Committee for review. It is expected to be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation early next month. The principle of the law is to protect the lives of workers and adopts a compulsory system. Insurance types are divided into two categories: injury insurance and health insurance.

Undoubtedly, this is a welcome measure for Chinese workers, whose lives are not guaranteed at all. Workers in society are the main creators of modern people's welfare and wealth, but their lives are often tragic among the people. Therefore, after many scholars' advocacy and workers' own struggles in the nineteenth century, most civilized countries have now established labor social insurance. Moreover, many countries have incorporated it into their constitutions as a major part of government policy.

The only thing that general industrialists pay attention to is the acquisition of profits, and they rarely pay attention to the improvement of labor conditions and safety facilities. The number of conflicts between laborers and employers due to such events is difficult to count. However, when it comes to Chinese industry, it is originally miserable to mention. The industry itself is not developed, so how can it withstand the exploitation of capitalists from various countries? Therefore, it is extremely difficult for general industrialists to obtain their own profits, let alone provide relief to workers when they are sick. Now that it is protected by labor insurance, it can be considered a great merit and a blessing for people's livelihood, no matter what.

However, although the main form of "labor insurance" adopts the state's "compulsory system" to take advantage of the situation, its ultimate goal is to promote the improvement of the labor environment, pay attention to safety facilities, and establish strict labor hygiene equipment in the society. Therefore, in addition to the implementation of laws and regulations, we must also promote the entire society to enable workers to enjoy the happiness of "insurance."

What's more, labor insurance should not only pay attention to injuries and diseases, but also to cultural facilities, unemployment relief, bereavement compensation, and old-age care. Some people may think that the former two are the most important for China at present and must be carried out gradually. Then we will wait and see.

Autumn Melody

— Rong

From the slanting wind and drizzle permeating the gray sky, from every weary cicada chirp, from the sunlight that fades a little every day, summer is quietly fading away. Sitting by the window with my collar open, gazing at the crisscrossing streets spread out before me, a feeling of "another year, another autumn breeze" wells up in my heart. The clamor and turmoil of summer have subsided, allowing the wind and rain to end everything that once shone with glory and splendor. It is like attending a sad funeral, seeing only withered wreaths and silently moving rows of monks in black robes, hearing only mourning music, and inevitably adding a stroke or two of gloomy oil paint to the bottom of my heart.

I still remember last year in early autumn, when a few patches of clear sky appeared after the new rain, and white clouds piled up into strange peaks in the sky. On a whim, I went to the suburbs to find Spanish architecture that matched the mood of autumn. In the vast fields, here was a patch of unfaded green, and there were toy-like scarlet villas. Occasionally, on quiet tree-lined roads, I could see lonely and melancholy young women walking slowly, holding small parasols, drifting by like a dream. I would half-heartedly watch their backs disappear into the autumn forest with a touch of melancholy. But now, even that mood is gone. The house is quiet, the person is thin, the smoke rings exhaled from the mouth are pale, and the mood is indifferent. I don't want to think about anything, I just want to go to the countryside to see the clear autumn pool and the egret-feather-like reed catkins.

Here, besides hearing a few cries of ice vendors, there are relatively few traces of autumn. In the countryside, the situation is different. The fields are filled with undulating waves of ripe wheat, and the setting sun shines on the backs of cattle, creating a dazzling golden light. The small river flows by like a conch shell, and the smoke from the cooking fires in the bronze-colored sky transforms into magical characters. There are the rustling of leaves, the sound of raindrops hitting the grass and trees, the sound of weak oars, and the sound of insects buzzing under the starry sky. The peace of the countryside, the purity of the heart, and the beauty of the season compose a silent chapter. And I, I will sit under an old tree, smoking a peaceful pipe, and gaze intently at the picturesque fields in the evening. No one will pay attention to me, except for the familiar geese and dogs.

But this hope is difficult to realize. When I have nothing to do, I sometimes bring a useless book, a park ticket, and my own unchanging silent temperament, and linger in the autumn park. A tired atmosphere hovers over the poetic ponds, and the French sycamores tremble in the late summer breeze. Birds peck at the soil after the new rain. I smell the breath of autumn. In the scarlet light of the setting sun, I sit on a long chair and watch the white clouds chasing each other in the sky, watch the faces of the tourists dyed red by the sunset, watch the branches swaying, watch the banana peels left by others on the ground, and watch the book in my hand and the old streetcar ticket that I accidentally found in the book. It's all beautiful. The weather is no longer hot, but it's not too cool. In the lonely tranquility, I seem to hear autumn calling me, and my imagination unfolds like brocade. I imagine that autumn should have beautiful flowers, dreams woven by fireflies, crickets comforting my loneliness, sweet roasted chestnuts, round and ripe grapes, a clear sky that evokes imagination, and a sense of ease all over my body, like removing shackles. All these embellishments drive away the gloomy mood of the entire season. I look forward to a little refreshing wind and rain to see how autumn's magic hand will change the universe. I want to see the power of autumn.

My expectations have not been in vain. From the slanting wind and drizzle permeating the gray sky, from every weary cicada chirp, from the sunlight that fades a little every day, autumn has quietly come.

Cicada

— Erhe

Sitting in the shade of a tree reading in the evening, I often unconsciously think of Huang Zhongze's line of poetry: "Even when the cicada swallows its voice, it still has a sound." Actually, it is not without reason. Firstly, since returning to my hometown, I have been listening to the cicada's song every day, which is very annoying to others but very interesting to me. Secondly, that line of poetry really expresses the feeling of my own heart as I approach "middle age."

Indeed, I have a special interest in cicadas. When I was young, because I grew up in the countryside, cicadas were my good companions all day long every summer. Under the scorching sun, I pinched reed heads and searched for spider webs all day long. When the spider silk on the reed heads was very, very thick, I would raise my head and look for cicadas in the big trees. Every time, I would always glue many cicadas and keep them in a cage. When the cicadas were first put in the cage, they just wanted to fly, always bumping from this side to that side, from that side to this side. After a long time, they would settle down. Hanging them on the beams or bed frames, they would naturally sing. At that time, of course, I was extremely happy, but my parents often threw my cage outside the door. I hated it. I couldn't find a reason to throw the cage outside the door.

Because I knew that cicadas ate dew, I would hang the cage outside at night. In this way, often for many days, many days, the cicadas were still alive and still singing with high spirits. When I was tired of playing, I would open the cage and catch one or two of them and let them fly away into the distance. Or I would tie a cicada to each end of a line and let them fly. It was very difficult for them to fly, but for this reason, I felt very satisfied. Not only that, I also liked to put the shell of some kind of grass over the cicada's eyes and let it fly. It flew very, very high. Sometimes, when the wind blew the shell off its eyes, it would fly into the green forest as if it had been saved. If the shell remained on its eyes forever, it would fly upward, upward forever, but sometimes it would suddenly fall down, probably because it was too tired or dizzy.

My parents told me that if I did this, I would be blind in the next life, but in fact, I was not afraid of this. Really, this way of playing made me feel too interested.

Page 22

Before the cicadas shed their shells, now I know to call it "cultivation." In the beginning, I only knew to call it "zhiliao". After every plum rain, the "cultivation" opens the mud, comes out of a small hole, and prepares to climb onto a tree to shed its shell. Because it was still early summer at that time, and the cicadas had not yet started singing, the "cultivation" was especially precious. Confined in the house, I only hoped that the plum rain would stop for a moment. When it stopped, I would go barefoot to find the small holes, carefully using my fingers to probe into each small hole like Columbus discovering a branch floating on the sea. After getting them, I would put them in a cage and wait for them to shed their shells, but it was never as good as gluing them with spider silk. Sometimes, when they had just shed half of their shell, I would become impatient and use my fingers to pull off the other half. As a result, the wings would always grow poorly. It was best to quietly sneak to every tree on a moonlit night, because at that time, there were often "cultivation" shedding their shells or already having shed their shells. The new cicada's wings had just grown well, and the color was pale lake blue, which was especially beautiful compared to those black-winged cicadas that were singing.

In addition to this, I also liked to find cicada shells. It was said that they could be used as medicine and sold to pharmacies in nearby towns. Although I never took them out to sell, I would always gather hundreds of pairs every summer and string them together with a thread into a long string, which was not as expensive as pearls when hung on the bamboo of the mosquito net, but it had the beauty of pearls.

However, I have already given these dreams to the next generation of children. In the evening, in the breeze of dusk, I no longer have the heart to guess the riddle that children are familiar with: "Living in the mud, climbing on the tall poplar, playing the flute in the daytime, drinking wine and enjoying the cool in the night." Hearing the cicada's song, I only unconsciously think of Huang Zhongze's line of poetry: "Even when the cicada swallows its voice, it still has a sound."

In the Hospital

— Ge Ren

When I woke up, the room was pitch black. So I reached behind me to turn on the light switch, but the place my fingers touched was a cold, hard wall, and my bed seemed to have been changed. This made me wonder if I was dreaming. I wanted to shout, because if I was really dreaming, I could suddenly wake up, or I could prove whether my suspicion was just overthinking. But the fact that my whole body was tied up like a soft rope, unable to move, was secondary to the fact that my throat was so blocked that I couldn't shout out a single word. So I opened my eyes and stared into the dark space, trying my best to calm myself down. I thought that there would always be some movement to confirm my current suspicions.

But the brain is something that can never be controlled by itself. Sometimes it is like a calm sea, and sometimes it is like a tumultuous sea. Now it was in such a situation. My mind was like a tangled mess of hemp, unable to find a beginning. Thinking of this and thinking of that, many forgotten, painful things vividly played out, without the slightest mercy, causing my body, which was tied up by a soft rope, to twitch painfully. My throat could no longer bear the pressure of that blockage. It was as if a breath of air was surging up from between my chest and brain, and it broke through that difficult pass. It turned out to be a cough. This made me completely think it over. When I got up this morning, I was a little agitated. I reluctantly wanted to go to the office, as if trying to squeeze onto a crowded streetcar. Squeezing and bumping, my legs softened. After that, perhaps I fainted. Then, I touched the cold, hard wall again with my hand, touched the edge of the bed, and touched my forehead. My forehead was burning like fire. Undoubtedly, after I fainted, I was moved to some place. After so many thoughts swirled in my mind, I calmed down. Actually, I already felt a faint pain in my temples. I could no longer think of anything. But since I had confirmed that I wasn't dreaming, where am I sleeping? I still wanted to know this second question. Since I couldn't move my body, my hands could still do a little work. I gathered my strength and knocked on the cold wall. Sure enough, a series of clicking leather shoe sounds came to my ears. When they stopped, the light in the room came on. "In the hospital," I immediately understood. The lady in white, wearing a white hat, shook her head at me with a pitying attitude. A thermometer, I could see it clearly, was placed under my tongue. I closed my eyes, because I thought of whether there would be any changes in my office after I, such a person, disappeared, which was the biggest problem for me.

The nurse checked the thermometer and told me that my temperature had dropped and that I would get better if I rested well. I wanted to wait for her to tell me something more, but she turned around and was about to leave. At that time, I called out rudely. "Who brought me to the hospital?" She first forbade me from speaking loudly, and then she told me the story as if she were telling a story: Several people brought you here this morning. They said you fainted at the streetcar station. After our doctor examined you, they found the place where you work in your pocket. They called and they replied that you are their employee, but she stared at me for a long time:

"They said you are single!"

She seemed to be waiting for me to answer with disbelief. The sincerity of a stranger excited me. I wanted to tell her the story that had just swirled in my mind, perhaps she could show me a little sympathy! But I nodded to her, gave her a smile, and closed my eyes, letting this story be preserved forever in my mind.

Chen Ruilin and Chen Yunlin's Falling Golden Fan

Oriental (1020) 1:00 PM to 2:00 PM

Page 23

Page 24

Page 25

Opening "Dream of the Red Chamber - Zijuan"

The moonlight slants on the azalea branches. Outside the window, cuckoos cry blood-stained sand. Little Zijuan's loyalty is as heavy as iron. She was originally a maidservant at Jia's mother's hall. Only because Lin Gu Ye was ill in Yangzhou, she accompanied the young lady to the canal office. Therefore, the mistress and servant have a deep affection like sisters. We pity you, cherish you, and you pity us. With her ice-like skin, jade-like bones, and clever nature, she is a flower in her prime at the age of fifteen or sixteen. She often accompanies Daiyu in the Xiao Xiang Pavilion. Sometimes, she earnestly advises the foolish Bao Yu to stop complaining and weeping. Sometimes, she prepares strong decoctions with a sigh. Sometimes, she idly listens to the parrot reciting poetry. Sometimes, she accompanies the beautiful girl alone, counting fallen flowers. Sometimes, she wipes the incense burner and speaks her heart. Sometimes, she holds a zither and asks for words while offering tea. Look at her, testing the foolish Bao Yu's infatuation. This is her pure loyalty and love for her mistress. Who knew the red thread would be secretly cut by others? The road to Mount Tiantai is distant, covered by white clouds. Later, the pearl sinks, the jade shatters, and the hairpins break. The beauty of youth is buried in the white sand. She feels that the foolish Bao Yu is not unfaithful, and she vows never to hold a pipa for the rest of her life. She accompanies Xichun, chanting Buddhist scriptures in the blue lamp, understanding the secular world and wishing to become a nun. The blue clothes and red sleeves are exchanged for a cassock.

Chen Ruilin and Chen Yunlin's Mao Family Painting

City Music (1340) 5:45 PM to 6:30 PM

Opening "Zhuang Zixiu" (General Outline)

Admirable Zhuang Zixiu in his days. His nature was born proud of nobles. He once served as a minor official in the melon garden. He removed his hat and retired to enjoy himself. In his dream, butterflies fluttered. Doubting if it's real or not, unrestrained. Waking up, he is still Zhuang Zhou. Whenever he meets noble and wise men, he thinks of asking them about the Tao. He met Laozi and the green ox in the clouds. Idly reading a volume of the Nanhua Jing. Roaming freely, strange autumn. Parables are nothing but illusions. Don't seek fame and profit for life. Hui Shi, a true confidant, came and went. They talked to each other with great spirits. Unexpectedly, his wife fell ill. Ginseng and Lingzhi were taken daily but were difficult to cure. The clothing, coffin, and outer coffin were prepared and placed in advance. He laughed loudly while singing a tune with a broken basin. Hui Shi didn't know what this meant. Why was the broken string not sad? Saying that it is good for her husband to bury her after death. She can avoid shame from the world for the rest of her life. When I die, my wife will definitely remarry. The fields, gardens, carriages, and horses will be taken by others. From now on, get rid of the burdens of the mortal world. From now on, my body will be like an unburdened boat. Vague, ethereal, and truly open-minded. Even if I don't become an immortal, I'll still be carefree. The blue sea and green mountains are free to roam. Wanting to find a companion like Chang Sang Gong. He is not similar to ordinary Taoists. How can he hope to refine pills and achieve immortality?

Movie News

Half a Week in Tianyi

Reprint of "Mother" Sheet Music

Tianyi's new sound film "Mother" is about to be completed. Fan Xuepeng plays the role of the mother, and her acting skills have achieved great success. The film includes two new songs, "Mother Song" and "Farewell Song." Exquisite sheet music has already been printed and distributed to all sectors. The first edition of 7,000 copies was completely given away in less than ten days due to the large number of people requesting the music. They had to reprint it to meet the enthusiasm of those requesting the sheet music from all walks of life. (Address for requesting gifts: Propaganda Department of Tianyi Film Company, No. 232 Ganse Dong Road, French Concession, Shanghai)

Li Yihe Goes to Japan for Inspection

Li Yihe, the distribution director of the business department of Tianyi Company, recently went to Japan on the President Coolidge yesterday afternoon to inspect the film industry, because he saw that the domestic film industry was not prosperous, while the Japanese film industry was booming. He plans to conduct a thorough investigation of the film production situation and the current screening situation in Japan. It is said that he expects to stay in Japan for one month.

Lu Lixia is Out of Danger

Lu Lixia, a basic actress of Tianyi, recently gave birth in a hospital and was once in danger. People who admire Lu's art and friends in the circle have sent letters and telegrams of condolences and are very concerned about Lu's illness. According to Wang Yinmei's report to the company, Lu has been out of danger and gave birth to a boy a few days ago. However, due to excessive bleeding, she needs a longer period of recuperation. Therefore, I specially tell friends who care about Miss Lu truthfully.

Even a Fool Has a Fool's Luck

Ge Furong, the big man of Tianyi, recently had good luck and won a fifth prize in the aviation lottery, totaling fifty yuan. Ge was overjoyed, even more so than on the eve of his wedding. Everyone said that even a fool has a fool's luck.

Public Announcement by the Initiators of Mr. Nie Er's Memorial Service

Time: 9:30 AM on the 16th of this month (Friday)

Location: Jin Cheng Grand Theater, Guizhou Road

Participants: Anyone can enter, but please pay attention: the seating in Jin Cheng is limited. Please go back if the seats are full. There will be no exceptions made at the time. Participants are requested to arrive early.

Supplementary Notice from the Organizing Committee: (1) Initiators are requested to bring a preparation fee of one yuan when attending the meeting. (2) Condolence banners and couplets from all walks of life are requested to be sent before the 14th to (1) Diantong Company, Jingzhou Road or (2) Jin Cheng Grand Theater, Guizhou Road for collection.
